## Missions
1. Reference consumed-table boundary precompute: eliminate repeated whole-prefix table extent scans when stripping consumed reference definitions.
2. Reference candidate guards: skip expensive reference-collection checks on lines that cannot contain reference, table, quote, HTML, fence, list, or setext syntax.
3. Nested reference allocation pass: reduce temporary `Vec<String>` and `Vec<&str>` churn in nested blockquote/list reference harvesting while preserving scope.
4. Paragraph classifier fast paths: make `line_is_paragraph_text` and related block-starter checks return early with byte-level predicates before full semantic detectors.
5. Spanned parser span collection: apply the proven reference/table boundary optimization to source-span collection and diagnostics path.
6. Inline parse allocation reduction: target `inline_parse` object churn without changing delimiter pairing, link resolution, or autolink behavior.
7. Table parser row splitting: reduce allocation/copying in GFM table splitting and delimiter validation.
8. List splitting body storage: reduce list-item body string cloning while preserving lazy-continuation, looseness, and task-list semantics.
9. Line split/source line storage: evaluate line splitting and source-line span storage for avoidable allocations in parser-large and spanned parse.
10. PDF layout hot loop: target text measurement, paragraph item construction, or layout scratch reuse in the `layout` stage.
11. PDF page content generation: reduce buffer churn and repeated formatting in `page_content_stream_generation`.
12. PDF stream compression policy: check compression thresholds and staging to avoid work where Flate cannot win.
13. PDF object serialization writers: target deterministic append writers in `pdf_object_serialization_total` and xref/trailer emission.
14. Hyphenation corpus path: look for a scored cache/layout opportunity in the 29.779 ms p95 `hyphen-corpus` scenario.
15. Final reprofile and guardrail pass: rerun focused baselines, update artifacts/proofs, and only accept changes that clear behavior and variance gates.

- Isomorphism: a fitting trailing forced line has badness zero and demerits one; without interior hard breaks or rewarded negative penalties, any earlier break adds at least one non-negative-cost line before the same final forced line, so the single full line is the unique optimal DP result. The negative-penalty regression test keeps that exceptional path on the dynamic program.

- Isomorphism: the previous inner loop also attempted the root transition first for every start and applied terminal values immediately after each successful transition; the new structure performs the same transitions and score updates while avoiding the extra root-node loop setup for absent starts.

## Completed Passes
### Pass 1: HTML heading-id allocation
- Mission: reduce `html-large` heading-id slug/collision allocation overhead in clean `src/html.rs`.
- Root cause: heading rendering kept two deterministic maps/sets (`used_heading_ids` plus `next_heading_suffix`) and cloned each accepted id so it could both store and return the same string.
- Change: replaced the dual structure with one deterministic `BTreeMap<String, usize>` that tracks emitted ids and next suffixes, and changed heading rendering to push the accepted id directly into the HTML output buffer.
- Correctness: preserves collision behavior for generated ids and later literal headings, including `foo`, `foo-2`, duplicate `foo`, and empty-heading fallback ids.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/html.rs`; `cargo test html::tests --lib`; worker also reported `cargo test heading_ids_are_unique_non_empty_and_collision_safe --test smoke_test`, `cargo check --all-targets`, `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`, `cargo test`, and checksum comparison of regenerated `html-large.html` against the baseline artifact.
- Directional performance: worker's focused release sample measured `html-large` p95 at 31.316 ms versus fourth-loop baseline 35.940 ms.
- Commit: `9c169f3`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 2: HTML task/list formatting
- Mission: remove avoidable temporary formatting work in task-list rendering while preserving exact HTML bytes.
- Root cause: every task-list item allocated a temporary `String` through `format!` only to splice the optional ` checked` attribute marker into a fixed literal.
- Change: replaced the `format!` call with direct `push_str` calls and a conditional append for the checked marker.
- Correctness: emitted task-list HTML is byte-identical because the same literal fragments and optional marker are appended in the same order.
- Verification: `cargo test --lib html::tests`; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported `cargo fmt --check -- src/html.rs`, task-checkbox focused tests, byte comparisons for regenerated `html-large` and `html-code-heavy` goldens, `cargo check --all-targets`, `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`, and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: no independent p95 claimed for this tiny allocation removal; expected benefit scales with task-list item count inside HTML-heavy documents.
- Commit: `74aebe0`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 3: HTML table and block emission
- Mission: trim repeated small alignment lookups in table/block emission without changing rendered HTML.
- Root cause: `render_table` recomputed the same column alignment attribute for every header and body cell by indexing `table.align` and mapping `Align` to a style fragment inside each cell loop.
- Change: precompute per-table alignment fragments once and route header/body rows through a shared table-cell emitter that appends precomputed attributes for aligned columns and emits no attribute for malformed extra direct-AST cells.
- Correctness: preserves the previous `Align::None` fallback for cells beyond the alignment vector and keeps all literal table wrapper, row, header, and body markup byte-identical.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/html.rs`; `cargo test --lib html::tests`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance gfm_table`; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported smoke tests, golden HTML/PDF output tests, byte comparisons for regenerated `html-large` and `html-code-heavy`, `cargo check --all-targets`, `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`, and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: worker's short comparable release sample measured `html-large` p95 at 28.725 ms versus fourth-loop baseline 35.940 ms; `html-code-heavy` stayed within variance.
- Commit: `1d9e95a`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 4: HTML inline text escaping
- Mission: reduce inline renderer escape allocation overhead on large and code-heavy HTML documents.
- Root cause: text-node render paths called `escape_text`, which allocated a temporary owned string for escaped text and then copied it into the caller's output buffer.
- Change: added `push_escaped_text` to stream escaped text directly into the existing HTML buffer, and used it for inline text/code/html fallback, code blocks without highlighting, escaped raw HTML blocks, invalid-image alt text, and highlighted code spans.
- Correctness: preserves the text escape set (`&`, `<`, `>`) and leaves attribute escaping (`escape_attr`) untouched, so link/image attributes and title handling keep their stricter quote escaping.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/html.rs`; `cargo test --lib html::tests`; `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens`; `cargo test --test smoke_test html`; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported parser conformance/metamorphic HTML tests, direct showcase HTML byte comparison, `cargo check --all-targets`, `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`, and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: no post-change p95 claimed in this pass; the improvement is a mechanically proven allocation reduction on escaped text paths.
- Commit: `e5a2a57`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 5: HTML font-usage collection
- Mission: reduce `BTreeSet` churn while collecting deterministic HTML embedded-font subset characters.
- Root cause: each font usage slot inserted every character into a `BTreeSet<char>`, making large mostly-ASCII documents pay tree lookup/insertion overhead for a small fixed ASCII universe.
- Change: replaced each slot with `FontCharSet`, using a `[bool; 128]` bitmap for ASCII and a `BTreeSet<char>` only for non-ASCII, then materializing chars in Unicode scalar order before calling the font subsetter.
- Correctness: ASCII chars are emitted in ascending scalar order and all non-ASCII chars remain in `BTreeSet` order, preserving the old `BTreeSet<char>` subset input order and deterministic font bytes.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/html.rs`; `cargo test --lib html::tests`; `cargo test --test smoke_test default_html_embeds_deterministic_subset_font_faces`; `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported regenerated `html-large`, `html-code-heavy`, and `html-showcase` checksum matches, `cargo fmt --check`, `cargo check --all-targets`, `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`, and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: worker's focused 5-iteration sample measured `html-large` p95 at 22.872 ms versus fourth-loop baseline 35.940 ms.
- Commit: `fd81945`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 6: HTML default CSS assembly
- Mission: reduce remaining default stylesheet/color-token assembly allocations while preserving exact CSS bytes.
- Root cause: default CSS generation built temporary strings for the light `:root` color block, the dark-mode color block, and each sanitized color token before copying them into the final stylesheet buffer.
- Change: stream light and dark color variable blocks directly into the final CSS buffer, and stream sanitized CSS token bytes directly for each variable value while keeping a test-only `css_token` wrapper for the sanitizer contract.
- Correctness: preserves the previous color-token filter, `initial` fallback, light/dark block ordering, and dark-mode wrapper whitespace; golden output and theme tests cover the full emitted stylesheet.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/html.rs`; `cargo test --lib html::tests`; `cargo test --test theme_test`; `cargo test --test golden_output rendered_html_and_pdf_match_committed_goldens`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `git diff --check -- src/html.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported smoke HTML tests, baseline artifact checksum verification, `cargo check --all-targets`, and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: worker's short after sample measured `html-showcase` p95 at 0.589 ms and `html-large` p95 at 21.596 ms, including prior fourth-loop HTML commits.
- Commit: `19dc635`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 7: Compression stored-path emission
- Mission: reduce allocation/copy work in stored DEFLATE fallback while preserving zlib validity and fixed-vs-stored selection.
- Root cause: stored fallback collected all `data.chunks(65535)` into a temporary vector, then built a separate raw stored DEFLATE body and copied that body into the final zlib output buffer.
- Change: added direct stored-block append helpers that write BFINAL/BTYPE=00 headers, LEN/NLEN, and chunk bytes directly into the final output buffer; kept a test-only `deflate_stored` wrapper to pin the stored length contract.
- Correctness: empty input still emits one empty final stored block, multi-block input marks only the final block with `BFINAL=1`, and `deflate_stored_len` now shares the `STORED_BLOCK_MAX` constant with the writer.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/compress.rs`; `cargo test --lib compress::tests`; `cargo check --all-targets`; local `compress-corpus.lengths` comparison against the fourth-loop baseline, SHA-256 `1ce5b05d2d0d0ad5912479bb1cefeb9f987bdda9b8fbcda575e8c8d9b03f3a87`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: no durable p95 win claimed; fixed compression remains dominant before the stored fallback is selected, so this pass is primarily an allocation/copy reduction.
- Commit: `6aeca02`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 8: Compression match finder
- Mission: reduce hash-chain match-length overhead in `compress-corpus` while preserving zlib validity and compressed-output bytes.
- Root cause: the hash-chain walker called `match_len` for candidates that could not beat the current best match, causing byte-by-byte comparisons on short collisions that would be rejected anyway.
- Change: before calling `match_len`, probe the byte at `best_len`; if `data[cand + best_len] != data[pos + best_len]`, the candidate cannot produce `len > best_len`, so the walker advances to the previous candidate without changing ordering or tie-breaking.
- Correctness: the probe is guarded by `best_len < max_match`, and the encoder only accepts strictly longer matches, so skipped candidates could not affect emitted matches or compressed output.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/compress.rs`; `cargo test --lib compress::tests`; `cargo check --all-targets`; local `compress-corpus.lengths` comparison against the fourth-loop baseline, SHA-256 `1ce5b05d2d0d0ad5912479bb1cefeb9f987bdda9b8fbcda575e8c8d9b03f3a87`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: local 5-iteration `compress-corpus` p95 was 6.340 ms versus fourth-loop baseline 8.647 ms; worker's after sample reported 6.376 ms p95.
- Commit: `fa01b9a`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 9: Compression fixed-code emission
- Mission: reduce repeated fixed Huffman bit/code work while preserving exact compressed bytes.
- Root cause: every literal/length/distance emission recomputed the fixed Huffman code path and reversed canonical code bits at runtime, even though fixed DEFLATE code tables never change.
- Change: build compile-time fixed literal/length and distance tables in the pre-reversed bit orientation needed by the LSB-first `BitWriter`, and emit those values through `write_reversed_huffman`.
- Correctness: the tables are generated from the same canonical `litlen_code` and `reverse_bits` logic, match selection and stored fallback are untouched, and `compress-corpus.lengths` remains byte-identical.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/compress.rs`; `cargo test --lib compress::tests`; `cargo check --all-targets`; local `compress-corpus.lengths` comparison against the fourth-loop baseline, SHA-256 `1ce5b05d2d0d0ad5912479bb1cefeb9f987bdda9b8fbcda575e8c8d9b03f3a87`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: local 5-iteration `compress-corpus` p95 was 5.552 ms versus pass 8 local 6.340 ms and fourth-loop baseline 8.647 ms; worker reported 5.665 ms p95.
- Commit: `313b7b8`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 10: Compression stored-block inflate
- Mission: improve decode/support paths without relaxing zlib validation or PNG/PDF image safety.
- Root cause: stored-block inflate is byte-aligned after `LEN/NLEN`, but copied each payload byte through `br.bits(8)`, doing eight bit-reader steps per raw byte.
- Change: added `BitStream::aligned_bytes` and changed the stored-block payload path to extend the output directly from the aligned input slice.
- Correctness: the existing order remains alignment, `LEN/NLEN`, `max_out`, input-bounds check, payload copy, final-body-byte validation, and Adler-32 verification; truncated bodies and trailing body bytes still fail.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/compress.rs`; `cargo test --lib compress::tests`; `cargo test --test pdf_test png`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported baseline artifact checksum verification, `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`, and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: this targets stored-block decode paths used by zlib/PNG support rather than the encode-heavy `compress-corpus` scenario, so no encode p95 claim is made.
- Commit: `f74f8bb`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 11: Parser scanner URL-prefix gating
- Mission: reduce low-hanging parser/reference-collection scanner work after the mid-loop profile showed `parser-large` as the leading non-PDF clean hotspot.
- Root cause: `scan_markdown_line` checked `www.`, `http`, and `://` with slice `starts_with` probes at every byte, even though only `w`, `h`, and `:` can start those prefixes.
- Change: added `maybe_url_prefix_at` to gate the existing prefix checks by the current byte before calling `starts_with`, preserving conservative `maybe_autolink` behavior with fewer probes on ordinary text.
- Correctness: every previous positive URL-prefix case still runs the same `starts_with` check, and scanner/parser conformance tests pin the conservative line-classifier behavior.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/scanner.rs`; `cargo test --test scanner_test`; `cargo test --lib parse::`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance`; `cargo check --all-targets`; local 3-iteration `parser-large` proof with HTML byte comparison against the mid-loop artifact; `git diff --check -- src/scanner.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo test`.
- Directional performance: local 3-iteration `parser-large` p95 was 36.352 ms versus mid-loop 40.683 ms; treat as directional due to the short run.
- Commit: `3c5007c`
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE

### Pass 12: Hyphenation lowercase scratch avoidance
- Mission: reduce low-hanging hyphenation overhead after the mid-loop profile showed `hyphen-corpus` as the next clean non-PDF hotspot.
- Root cause: `Hyphenator::hyphenation_points_into_scratch` copied already-lowercase ASCII words into `hyphen_lower` before exception lookup and trie scoring, even though their normalized form was identical to the input.
- Change: use the original `&str` for all-lowercase ASCII words and fill `hyphen_lower` only when uppercase normalization is required.
- Correctness: non-ASCII and non-alphabetic words still return early, uppercase words still normalize through the same lowercase buffer, and exception lookup/trie scoring/legal-point filtering receive identical bytes.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check -- src/layout.rs`; `cargo test --test layout_test hyphen`; `cargo check --all-targets`; local 10-iteration `hyphen-corpus` proof with `hyphen-corpus.points` byte-identical to the mid-loop artifact, SHA-256 `e8caf211e32abbec328e65e70125da72e5022435cda24dffb5d1cf0908e33861`; `git diff --check -- src/layout.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; worker also reported `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings` and `cargo test`.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Arc Path Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T05:36:36Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Renderer change: dependency-free SVG path parsing now lowers `A/a` elliptical arc commands into one or more cubic Bezier segments using the SVG endpoint-to-center algorithm, instead of collapsing arcs to straight lines. This is an isolated quality/correctness lever for real SVG diagrams and preserves the existing cubic PDF drawing path.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Transform Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T05:45:55Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Root cause: the dependency-free SVG parser preserved paint/visibility/filter style state through `<g>` nesting, but it ignored `transform` attributes entirely. Generated diagram SVGs commonly use group and element transforms, so ignoring them rendered shapes and labels in the wrong coordinates even when all paint and path commands were supported.
- Renderer change: added a compact affine `SvgTransform` matrix, parsed common transform-list functions (`matrix`, `translate`, `scale`, `rotate`, `skewX`, `skewY`), composed group and element transforms in SVG source order, scoped transformed shape emission with local PDF `cm` graphics-state wrappers, and applied transformed anchor points/scales to SVG text placement.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_transform_attributes_apply_to_vector_shapes` pins direct element transforms, nested group+element composition, and CSS-style `transform:` declarations at the emitted PDF operator level.
- Audit sweep: `ubs . --format=jsonl` completed, but the default output was category-level rather than file-location-level. The high-signal JS critical category did not reproduce against repository JS with targeted secret/token comparison searches; DOM listener findings were confined to the static WASM demo script, whose required elements are already null-checked at startup.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_transform_attributes_apply_to_vector_shapes --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a real SVG renderer correctness gap found during the fellow-agent review while keeping the core dependency-free and preserving the existing AST/theme/render architecture.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG CSS Stroke/Dash Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T06:15:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `examples/showcase-mermaid.mmd`, `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, `examples/showcase.md`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Root cause: the dependency-free SVG path could parse direct paint attributes, but realistic generated SVGs also rely on simple stylesheet classes for stroke behavior. Without class-level `stroke-dasharray`, `stroke-dashoffset`, `stroke-linecap`, and `stroke-linejoin`, dashed diagram relationships could silently render as solid strokes or leak dash state into later shapes. Fresh-eyes review then found a second issue in the initial CSS subset: naive brace scanning could treat rules nested inside `@media` or `@supports` blocks as unconditional top-level class rules.
- Renderer change: added a small dependency-free CSS subset for simple `.class { ... }` SVG rules, class-list matching in source order, partial style patches, dash-pattern parsing, line-cap/line-join parsing, and PDF stroke option emission. Dashed elements now get local graphics-state wrappers so PDF dash state cannot leak into following solid elements. CSS rule scanning now matches complete blocks, skips conditional at-rule blocks as opaque, and still handles ordinary class rules after semicolon-terminated at-statements such as `@import`.
- Integration change: regenerated the showcase SVG from `/dp/frankenmermaid` after changing the final Mermaid edge to `G -.-> E`; updated the visible Markdown source block to match the rendered diagram.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_css_class_stroke_styles_apply_to_vector_shapes` pins class-applied dash/cap/join operators, verifies later solid strokes do not inherit a dash, verifies direct dash-offset/cap/join attributes still work, verifies a class rule after `@import` still applies, and verifies nested conditional class rules do not override the normal PDF rendering path.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` with `--pdf-image showcase-mermaid.svg=examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` into `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-css-dash-atrules-20260706T061035Z/showcase.pdf`, rasterized a copied PDF with Ghostscript to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-css-dash-atrules-20260706T061035Z/showcase-*.png`, and inspected pages 3 and 4. The frankenmermaid diagram is readable, the SVG asset-to-PDF edge is visibly dashed with aligned arrowhead, labels remain legible, shadows stay subtle, the source block shows `G -.-> E`, and syntax highlighting remains visible.
- Verification: `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo test pdf_svg_css_class_stroke_styles_apply_to_vector_shapes --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG styling correctness gap for frankenmermaid output while keeping the renderer dependency-free. The active goal is still not complete because "world-class SVG renderer" remains broader than this focused subset.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Fill Rule Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T06:28:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Root cause: the dependency-free SVG renderer treated every filled path with PDF's default nonzero winding rule. Real SVG icons, logos, and diagram assets commonly use `fill-rule="evenodd"` or CSS `fill-rule: evenodd` to cut holes from compound paths; ignoring it turns rings, counters, and nested subpaths into solid blobs in PDFs.
- Renderer change: added an inherited `SvgFillRule`, parsed `fill-rule` from presentation attributes, inline `style`, and simple CSS class rules, and mapped filled shapes to PDF's `f*` / `B*` even-odd paint operators when requested. Shadow fallback also uses `f*` for filled even-odd shapes so the fallback remains shape-consistent.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_evenodd_fill_rule_uses_pdf_even_odd_paint_operators` pins CSS `fill-rule: evenodd` to `f*`, attribute `fill-rule="evenodd"` with stroke to `B*`, and explicit `fill-rule: nonzero` to the default `f` operator.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_evenodd_fill_rule_uses_pdf_even_odd_paint_operators --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a compact but important SVG correctness step toward high-fidelity dependency-free vector rendering. The active goal remains open because broader SVG coverage such as gradients, clipping, masks, nested text spans, and richer CSS selector support is still not complete.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Gradient Paint Fallback
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T06:40:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Root cause: the dependency-free SVG renderer skipped `<defs>` and treated most `url(#...)` paint servers as `none`, except for one hardcoded frankenmermaid gradient id. Real SVGs commonly use `linearGradient` or `radialGradient` for fills and strokes; dropping those paints makes icons, logos, and diagrams invisible or materially less polished in PDF output.
- Renderer change: added a small gradient paint registry that scans simple `linearGradient` / `radialGradient` definitions, parses `stop` colors from attributes and inline stop styles, handles offsets and stop opacity deterministically, and resolves `url(#id)` fills/strokes to a weighted representative vector color. Missing paint servers can now honor SVG fallback colors such as `url(#missing) #00ff00` instead of always dropping paint.
- Scope note: this is intentionally a deterministic vector fallback, not full PDF shading resources. It keeps shapes visible and color-coherent without adding dependencies or rasterizing, while leaving true gradient shadings as future renderer work.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_gradient_paints_get_deterministic_vector_fallback_colors` pins defs-based gradient fills, CSS class gradient strokes, and missing-paint fallback colors at the emitted PDF operator level.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_gradient_paints_get_deterministic_vector_fallback_colors --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes another concrete SVG renderer quality gap for dependency-free PDF output. The active goal remains open because full "world-class" SVG coverage still requires deeper features such as true PDF gradients, clipping, masks, nested text spans, and richer CSS selector support.

## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG Clip Path Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T06:41:16Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review scope: traced the recently modified dependency-free SVG-to-PDF path through defs scanning, style cascade, inherited group styles, shape emission, selectable SVG text emission, and the `/dp/frankenmermaid` SVG renderer. The frankenmermaid source has explicit `clipPath` / `clip-path="url(#...)"` support for scene output, but franken_markdown had no clip-path registry or PDF clipping emission.
- Root cause: the main SVG traversal intentionally skips `<defs>` to keep unsupported paint servers and scripts out of the element stream. Gradients had a separate registry, but clip paths did not, so any generated SVG relying on rectangular/path scene clips silently painted outside its intended bounds. SVG text takes a separate PDF text path to stay selectable, so clipping also had to be wired there rather than only to shape emission.
- Renderer change: added a bounded `SvgClipPath` registry for `<clipPath>` definitions, with path, rect, circle, ellipse, and polygon geometry lowered into existing `SvgPathOp`s. Parsed `clip-path` from CSS class rules, presentation attributes, and inline styles; preserved inherited group clipping; supported `clip-rule` / `fill-rule` via PDF `W` and `W*`; scoped clipping with `q/Q`; and mapped clipped SVG labels into PDF page-space clipping paths while keeping the text selectable.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_clip_paths_apply_native_pdf_clipping` pins frankenmermaid-style transformed group clipping, CSS-applied even-odd clipping, and clipped selectable SVG labels at the emitted PDF operator level.
- UBS note: `ubs . --format=jsonl` completed to `/tmp/fmd-ubs-pass1.jsonl` and returned aggregate category counts without actionable file/line findings. The high-signal fix above came from source tracing plus the concrete frankenmermaid clip-path contract.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_clip_paths_apply_native_pdf_clipping --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a real cross-project SVG/PDF correctness gap while keeping the core dependency-free and WASM-safe. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG coverage still includes deeper features such as true PDF gradient shadings, masks, richer CSS selectors, and more complete SVG text layout.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG CSS Variable Paint Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T06:49:49Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the completed fourth optimization loop remains the current performance handoff: `pdf-large` is still the dominant scenario at 334.406 ms p95, with PDF `layout` at 268.855 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 44.998 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.897 ms p95. This pass is not a speed claim; it advances the explicit frankenmermaid/SVG-renderer requirement.
- Root cause: real frankenmermaid SVG output includes CSS custom properties such as `--fm-edge-color`, `--fm-text-color`, and chained `var(...)` definitions in `<style>`. The dependency-free SVG renderer could parse literal `fill` / `stroke` colors and simple CSS class rules, but `var(...)` paint values failed to resolve, so class-styled SVGs could silently lose strokes/fills or gradient stop colors unless frankenmermaid also emitted direct literal attributes.
- Renderer change: added a bounded custom-property table for SVG `<style>` blocks, deterministic first-declaration-wins resolution for static PDF output, recursive `var(--name)` and `var(--name, fallback)` resolution for paint values, support for nested fallback functions such as `rgba(...)`, and the same variable resolution for gradient stop colors before representative fallback colors are computed. No external CSS or SVG dependency was added.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_css_variables_resolve_paint_values` pins class-applied stroke via a variable chain, attribute fill via `var(..., #fallback)`, transparent paint via a custom property, gradient stop colors via custom properties, and nested `rgba(...)` fallback parsing.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` with the real `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` asset to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-css-vars-20260706T0648Z/showcase.pdf`, copied it to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-css-vars-20260706T0648Z/showcase.pdf`, rasterized page 3 with Ghostscript to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-css-vars-20260706T0648Z/showcase-page-1.png`, and visually inspected the image. The frankenmermaid diagram is visible and readable with boxes, curved edges, the dashed edge, labels, and the Mermaid source panel intact.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_css_variables_resolve_paint_values --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes another real-world frankenmermaid/SVG paint fidelity gap while preserving the dependency-free, deterministic renderer architecture. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG coverage still includes true PDF gradient shadings, masks, marker definitions, richer selector matching, and more complete SVG text layout.

## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG `<use>` Definitions
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T07:18:13Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review scope: traced the SVG parse path from raw tag scanning through defs registries, inherited style state, vector shape emission, selectable SVG text emission, and the existing frankenmermaid showcase asset. The renderer had grown support for gradients, clip paths, markers, CSS variables, transforms, arcs, and fill rules, but still ignored `<use>` elements entirely.
- Root cause: the main SVG traversal deliberately skips `<defs>` and had no separate registry for reusable SVG definitions. Any icon, sprite, diagram, or symbol-based SVG that renders visible content through `<use href="#...">` or `<use xlink:href="#...">` would silently drop that content in PDF output even though the referenced path/group geometry was otherwise within the supported renderer subset.
- Renderer change: added a bounded reusable-definition path that pre-scans actual `<use>` references, collects only referenced shape/group/symbol/text definitions, expands direct shapes and nested groups through the existing parser/style pipeline, preserves inherited `<use>` style plus x/y placement, supports `href`, `xlink:href`, and `url(#id)` fragments, and caps recursion/definition/body sizes to avoid malformed-SVG blowups. A fresh-eyes performance correction keeps no-`<use>` SVGs from allocating every id-bearing frankenmermaid group body.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_use_elements_expand_referenced_shapes_and_groups` pins direct path references, `xlink:href` group references, nested reusable groups, inherited group fill, explicit child stroke, and use-element x/y placement at the emitted PDF operator level.
- UBS note: `ubs . --format=jsonl` completed to `/tmp/fmd-ubs-review-20260706T070928Z.jsonl` and again emitted aggregate category counts without source-spanned actionable findings in `src/pdf.rs` or `tests/pdf_test.rs`; the fix came from manual first-principles tracing of the unsupported SVG reference model.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_use_elements_expand_referenced_shapes_and_groups --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `ubs --files=src/pdf.rs,tests/pdf_test.rs --format=jsonl .` (aggregate-only output, no source-spanned findings); `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a real SVG sprite/symbol correctness gap while keeping the renderer dependency-free and performant for the existing no-`<use>` frankenmermaid showcase. The active goal remains open because world-class SVG still includes richer selector matching, true PDF gradient shadings, masks, and more complete SVG text/tspan layout.

## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG `<tspan>` Text Runs
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T07:34:28Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review scope: traced the recently modified dependency-free SVG parser through top-level text elements, reusable `<use>` text definitions, nested reusable group bodies, style inheritance, fill visibility, selectable PDF text emission, text anchors, and the no-default/WASM-safe renderer constraints.
- Root cause: the SVG text parser stripped child tags and collapsed the whole `<text>` body into one PDF text run. That lost child `<tspan>` fill/font-size/positioning, made parent `fill="none"` hide otherwise visible child tspans, and made adjacent tspans stack at the same starting coordinate when no explicit `x` was supplied. Direct text around child tspans also needed careful whitespace handling so formatted SVG indentation stayed invisible while real boundary spaces remained meaningful.
- Renderer change: replaced the single-run text parser with bounded `parse_svg_text_elements` emission. Top-level, reusable-definition, and nested reusable-group text now produce separate selectable `SvgText` runs for visible direct text and child `<tspan>` nodes. Child tspans inherit parent style, can override fill/font-size/text-anchor/style, honor `x`, `y`, `dx`, and `dy` with simple SVG length units, and advance the current inline text point with a deterministic dependency-free approximation. Simple no-tspan text keeps the existing fast path and existing numeric `font-size` prefix behavior.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_tspan_children_render_as_separate_text_runs` pins parent `fill="none"` with visible child tspans, child fill/style overrides, `dy="1.5em"`, adjacent inline tspans without explicit `x`, and separate selectable PDF text runs. `svg_text_node_normalization_preserves_boundary_space_only_for_text` pins the whitespace rule for direct text nodes.
- UBS note: `ubs --files=src/pdf.rs,tests/pdf_test.rs --format=jsonl .` completed to `/tmp/fmd-ubs-tspan-final-20260706T073349Z.jsonl` and returned aggregate scanner/totals records only, with no source-spanned actionable finding in the touched files.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test svg_text_node_normalization_preserves_boundary_space_only_for_text --lib`; `cargo test pdf_svg_tspan_children_render_as_separate_text_runs --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `ubs --files=src/pdf.rs,tests/pdf_test.rs --format=jsonl .` (aggregate-only output, no source-spanned findings).

The active goal remains open because world-class SVG still includes deeper text layout, masks, richer selectors, and true PDF gradient shadings.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Partial Opacity And PDF ExtGState
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T07:47:04Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the completed optimization loop still identifies PDF work as the dominant remaining path: `pdf-large` p95 334.406 ms, with `layout` 268.855 ms, `page_content_stream_generation` 44.998 ms, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` 25.897 ms. This pass targets SVG/PDF content fidelity in that output path rather than claiming a speed win.
- Root cause: the SVG style model only used `opacity`, `fill-opacity`, and `stroke-opacity` to skip effectively zero-alpha content. Partially transparent real SVGs, including CSS class rules and rgba paints, rendered fully opaque in PDF output. Text labels had the same issue, and adding PDF transparency naively could have leaked alpha state into later page content.
- Renderer change: added first-class effective SVG alpha state for fill, stroke, and selectable SVG text; parsed numeric and percent opacity values from presentation attributes, inline styles, simple CSS class rules, CSS variables, gradient stops, and rgba paint values; emitted scoped `/GSaNNNNNNNN gs` operators around only affected SVG content; and auto-generated per-page `/ExtGState` resource dictionaries by scanning the already-built page stream. This keeps normal pages resource-free, avoids object-number churn, preserves deterministic output, and keeps the renderer dependency-free.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_partial_opacity_uses_native_pdf_extgstate_resources` pins percent `opacity`, `stroke-opacity`, `fill-opacity`, rgba fill alpha, class-rule rgba alpha, selectable text alpha, skipped `opacity=0` content, scoped content operators, and exact PDF `/ExtGState` resources.
- Integration proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` with the real `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` asset via `--pdf-image showcase-mermaid.svg=examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` into `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-opacity-20260706T074521Z/showcase.pdf` (59,723 bytes). Ghostscript refused project-path reads under its safe-mode policy, so the PDF was copied to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-opacity-20260706T074521Z/showcase.pdf` and rasterized there to `showcase-01.png` through `showcase-04.png`.
- Visual proof: inspected `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-opacity-20260706T074521Z/showcase-03.png` and `showcase-04.png`. The frankenmermaid diagram page is nonblank and readable, with vector-looking boxes, routed arrows, dashed edge, labels, and Mermaid source block intact; the following page still shows visible syntax highlighting and stable code/block layout.

## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG Native Linear Gradient Shadings
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T08:01:21Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review scope: re-read the fellow-agent SVG/PDF paint-server work from `<defs>` scanning through style inheritance, fill paint resolution, shape clipping, page content assembly, PDF resource serialization, and regression tests. The previous gradient pass kept shapes visible by flattening paint servers to representative colors, but simple linear-gradient fills could be represented natively in PDF without rasterizing or adding dependencies.
- Root cause: the renderer had gradient metadata only as fallback colors, and the newly added shading scaffolding initially risked a classic PDF wiring bug: content streams could say `/SG1 sh` while page resources lacked `/Shading`, making output viewer-dependent or invalid. A fresh-eyes review also found that exceeding the bounded per-page shading table must not silently reuse `/SG1`, because that would draw the wrong gradient.
- Renderer change: simple two-stop SVG `linearGradient` fills now register per-page PDF axial shading resources and paint the shape through a scoped clipping path plus `/SGn sh`. Unsupported gradient cases, including radial/stroke gradients and over-limit shading tables, fall back to the existing deterministic representative vector color path. The PDF buffer preallocation now accounts for shading resource dictionaries so SVG-heavy pages avoid predictable growth churn.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_gradient_paints_use_native_linear_shading_and_fallback_colors` pins the `/Shading` resource dictionary, endpoint colors, clipping-path shading paint, radial/stroke fallback colors, and missing paint-server fallback colors. `pdf_svg_css_variables_resolve_paint_values` now also pins CSS-variable gradient stop colors flowing into native shading endpoint colors rather than stale flat-color assertions.
- UBS note: `ubs --files=src/pdf.rs,tests/pdf_test.rs --format=jsonl .` completed to `/tmp/fmd-ubs-gradient-20260706T075900Z.jsonl` and returned only aggregate scanner/totals records, with no source-spanned actionable finding in the touched files.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Multi-Stop Linear Gradient Shadings
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T08:12:14Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the latest fourth-loop profile still leaves `pdf-large` as the dominant scenario at 334.406 ms p95, with PDF `layout` at 268.855 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 44.998 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.897 ms p95. This pass is a renderer fidelity pass for the frankenmermaid/SVG objective, not a new speed claim.
- Root cause: the native PDF shading path could represent only a two-color endpoint ramp. SVG `linearGradient` definitions with three or more stops were normalized for representative fallback color, but the actual native shading resource still collapsed visible output to first/last colors instead of preserving the intermediate stop colors that PDF can express natively with stitching functions.
- Renderer change: normalized SVG linear-gradient stops into a bounded, monotonic stop list before registering a native shading; clamped offsets into `[0, 1]`; deduplicated repeated offsets so PDF FunctionType 3 bounds remain valid; inserted implicit endpoint stops to preserve SVG extension semantics; kept the existing Type 2 function for two-stop gradients; and emitted Type 3 stitching functions for multi-stop gradients.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_multistop_linear_gradients_use_pdf_stitching_functions` pins the native `/Shading` resource, the Type 3 stitching function, the `/Bounds` and `/Encode` arrays, and the clipped `/SG1 sh` paint operation.
- Fresh-eyes note: duplicate offset stops are collapsed to the later color to avoid malformed non-increasing PDF stitching bounds. Exact SVG hard stops at a single offset remain a known future refinement, but the current behavior is deterministic, bounded, valid PDF, and materially more faithful than the previous endpoint-only ramp.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_multistop_linear_gradients_use_pdf_stitching_functions --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete multi-stop gradient correctness gap while preserving the dependency-free renderer architecture. The active goal remains open because world-class SVG coverage still includes masks, gradient transforms and spread methods, richer CSS selector matching, and more complete SVG text/layout semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Gradient Transform And Spread Semantics
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T08:17:55Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the prior optimization loop still identifies PDF rendering as the dominant remaining path. This pass is a renderer correctness improvement in the SVG/PDF paint-server path, not a measured speed claim.
- Root cause: the native linear-gradient shading path preserved stops but ignored two important SVG coordinate semantics. `gradientTransform` was dropped entirely, so transformed gradients painted along the wrong axis. Non-default `spreadMethod` values such as `repeat` or `reflect` were also treated as native PDF pad semantics through `/Extend [true true]`, which is deterministic but visibly wrong for SVGs that rely on repeating or reflecting ramps.
- Renderer change: added `gradientTransform` to the parsed linear-gradient model, reused the existing dependency-free SVG transform parser, transformed `userSpaceOnUse` gradient endpoints directly, transformed `objectBoundingBox` endpoints in normalized gradient space before mapping through the target element bounding box, and allowed native PDF shadings only for the default `pad` spread method. Unsupported spread modes now fall back to the existing representative vector color until a true repeating/reflecting shading implementation exists.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_linear_gradient_transform_and_spread_method_are_respected` pins transformed native `/Coords` for user-space gradients, transformed normalized object-bounding-box coordinates, clipped `/SGn sh` paint operations, and the fallback color path for `spreadMethod="repeat"`.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_linear_gradient_transform_and_spread_method_are_respected --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes another concrete SVG gradient correctness gap without adding dependencies or weakening WASM portability. The active goal remains open because exact repeat/reflect gradients, masks, richer CSS selectors, and deeper SVG text/layout support are still not complete.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Compound CSS Selectors
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T08:24:11Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the latest optimization evidence still points at PDF rendering as the dominant path. This pass is a renderer fidelity improvement in the SVG/PDF path, not a measured speed claim.
- Root cause: the dependency-free SVG stylesheet parser only accepted bare `.class` selectors. Real generated SVGs commonly use `#id`, type selectors, `tag.class`, `.a.b`, `tag#id.class`, and universal selectors for paint and stroke defaults. Those rules were silently ignored, so otherwise-supported SVG geometry could render with wrong fills, strokes, dash settings, or line joins. A naive expansion would also be wrong if it ignored CSS specificity, because an earlier `#id` rule must beat a later class rule.
- Renderer change: replaced the class-only rule key with a compact parsed selector model containing optional tag, optional id, class list, specificity, and source order. The matcher now supports simple compound selectors without combinators, applies matching rules by specificity and then source order, keeps presentation attributes and inline `style` as later overrides, and deliberately ignores unsupported descendant/attribute/pseudo selectors rather than treating them as unconditional rules.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_css_compound_selectors_apply_with_specificity` pins ID specificity over a later class rule, compound `.edge.dashed` class matching, `path.edge`, `rect#box.warning`, universal stroke options, type selectors for `line`, and ignored descendant selectors.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_css_compound_selectors_apply_with_specificity --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a broad real-SVG stylesheet fidelity gap while preserving the dependency-free parser boundary. The active goal remains open because masks, exact repeat/reflect gradients, richer selector families, and deeper SVG layout semantics remain incomplete.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Hard Mask Clipping Subset
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T08:31:26Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: PDF rendering remains the dominant measured path from the latest optimization loop. This pass is a renderer fidelity improvement in that PDF/SVG path rather than a speed claim.
- Root cause: the renderer had native clipping, alpha, gradients, markers, `<use>`, and text span support, but ignored SVG `<mask>` definitions and `mask="url(#...)"` references entirely. SVGs commonly use simple white filled mask geometry to reveal part of a shape or label; dropping the mask over-renders content outside the intended visible area.
- Renderer change: added a bounded hard-mask subset that scans `<mask>` definitions, lowers explicitly visible white/opaque filled path, rect, circle, ellipse, and polygon geometry into the existing `SvgClipPath` representation, ignores black or transparent mask children, and applies `mask` from presentation attributes, inline styles, and stylesheet rules as an additional scoped PDF clipping path for both vector shapes and selectable SVG text.
- Scope note: this is not a full PDF soft-mask implementation. It intentionally covers hard reveal masks that map exactly to native PDF clipping; luminance gradients, partial alpha masks, image masks, nested mask groups, mask transforms, and full SVG mask compositing remain future work.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_masks_apply_supported_hard_mask_geometry_as_pdf_clipping` pins white mask geometry becoming PDF `W`, black mask geometry not revealing content, even-odd white mask paths emitting `W*`, and CSS-applied masks clipping selectable SVG text.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_masks_apply_supported_hard_mask_geometry_as_pdf_clipping --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes the total absence of SVG mask handling for a common exact hard-mask subset while keeping the renderer dependency-free and PDF-native. The active goal remains open because full soft masks, exact repeat/reflect gradients, richer selectors, and deeper SVG layout semantics are still incomplete.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Gradient `href` Inheritance
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T08:49:40Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the existing profiling artifacts still rank PDF rendering as the dominant measured scenario, with prior loop notes listing `pdf-large` p95 at 334.406 ms and PDF layout/content-stream work as the main remaining cost. This pass advances the SVG/PDF renderer quality target in that hot output path; it is not claimed as a speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. Generated SVGs commonly define a base gradient and reuse it through `href`/`xlink:href`; the existing parser already had all local-gradient machinery, so resolving inherited definitions is a small, high-confidence fidelity improvement.
- Root cause: `parse_svg_gradient_paints` emitted a paint server only when a gradient element had local `<stop>` children. A derived `<linearGradient id="b" href="#a" .../>` had no local stops, so it was dropped entirely; shapes using `fill="url(#b)"` became invisible instead of inheriting the referenced stop list and unspecified coordinate attributes.
- Renderer change: gradient parsing now scans bounded gradient definitions first, including self-closing definitions, then resolves `href`/`xlink:href` inheritance with a recursion cap. Referenced attributes are inherited, local attributes override by name, local stop children override inherited stops only when present, and the resolved result flows through the existing representative-color and native PDF linear-shading paths. Cycles and missing references remain bounded and deterministic.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_linear_gradients_inherit_stops_and_attrs_via_href` pins xlink-based inheritance of `gradientUnits` and multi-stop colors, local `x1/y1/x2/y2` overrides, the native `/Shading` resource coordinates, the Type 3 stitching function, and clipped `/SG1 sh` painting.
- Isomorphism proof: ordering preserved because definitions are emitted in source order with duplicate paint ids ignored as before; tie-breaking unchanged for non-inherited gradients; floating-point behavior reuses existing parsing and PDF formatting; RNG is not involved; existing SVG tests continue to pass.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_linear_gradients_inherit_stops_and_attrs_via_href --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes another common generated-SVG paint-server gap while staying dependency-free and WASM-safe. The active goal remains open because full soft masks, exact repeat/reflect gradients, richer selector families, radial native shadings, and deeper SVG text/layout semantics remain incomplete.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Native Radial Gradient Shadings
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T09:06:19Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh directional profile bundle at `tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z/` reports `pdf-large` at 323.377 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. Stage evidence still ranks `layout` first at 246.082 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.081 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 26.202 ms p95. The profiled PDF byte proof passed via `golden/pdf-large-stages.jsonl` and `golden_checksums.txt`.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 4, effort 2, score 6.0. Real SVGs commonly use `radialGradient` for icons, glows, logos, and generated diagram accents. The parser and PDF shading resource path already supported gradient stops and native axial shading, so adding the exact circular radial subset was a compact high-confidence fidelity improvement in the active PDF/SVG hot path.
- Root cause: the gradient registry parsed `radialGradient` definitions only far enough to compute a representative fallback color. The native shading gate also explicitly required `linear.is_some()`, so even circular radial gradients that PDF can express exactly were flattened to solid vector fills.
- Renderer change: added a dependency-free `SvgRadialGradient` model, extended page shading resources with a `PdfShadingKind::Radial` variant emitted as PDF `/ShadingType 3`, and broadened native gradient paint references to include radial metadata. Native radial shading is intentionally conservative: it only accepts the default pad spread method, finite positive radii, focal circles contained within the outer circle, numeric user-space radii, and object-bounding-box mappings that remain circular after bbox scaling and `gradientTransform`. Unsupported elliptical or ambiguous cases keep the existing deterministic representative-color fallback.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_radial_gradients_use_native_pdf_shading_when_circular` pins a circular object-bounding-box radial gradient to `/ShadingType 3`, exact `[fx fy fr cx cy r]` coordinates, stop colors flowing into the PDF function, clipped `/SG1 sh` painting, and a non-square rectangular radial gradient falling back to the representative color instead of emitting wrong circular geometry.
- Isomorphism proof: non-radial gradients still flow through the existing axial or fallback paths; unsupported radial gradients preserve the previous representative vector color; shading resource names remain per-page insertion order; tie-breaking and duplicate gradient ids are unchanged; floating-point formatting uses the existing `pdf_num`/`pdf_fixed3` paths; RNG is not involved.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_radial_gradients_use_native_pdf_shading_when_circular --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z`; `RUSTFLAGS="-C force-frame-pointers=yes" cargo run --profile release-perf --example fmd_perf_harness -- --scenario pdf-large --iters 3 --out-dir tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z/golden`; `sha256sum -c tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z/golden_checksums.txt`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes another visible SVG/PDF paint-server limitation while keeping unsupported cases correct and dependency-free. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes exact repeat/reflect gradients, full soft masks, richer selector families, pattern/image paint servers, and deeper SVG layout semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG `currentColor` Cascade Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T09:13:01Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the active profile handoff remains the fresh `tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z/` bundle: `pdf-large` p95 323.377 ms over 3 release-perf iterations, with `layout` at 246.082 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.081 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 26.202 ms p95. This pass is a renderer-fidelity step in the hot PDF/SVG path, not a speed claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. `currentColor` is common in icon sets, generated SVGs, and themeable diagrams. The renderer already had a style cascade and paint application path, so adding inherited `color` state and current-color paint links was small and high-confidence.
- Root cause: `SvgStyle` tracked `fill` and `stroke` directly but had no inherited `color` property and no way to remember that a paint came from `currentColor`. As a result, stylesheet, presentation, and inline `currentColor` values were ignored and visible SVG paths/text fell back to black or inherited concrete paint instead of the intended theme color.
- Renderer change: added inherited `color` to `SvgStyle`, added `fill_current_color` and `stroke_current_color` links, parsed `color` from CSS rules, presentation attributes, and inline styles, resolved `fill` / `stroke` values of `currentColor` through existing `var(...)` handling, and updated currentColor-derived fill/stroke whenever a later color declaration changes the computed color. Concrete fills, strokes, gradients, and `none` clear the currentColor link and keep their previous behavior.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_current_color_resolves_through_cascade_and_inheritance` pins inherited class color driving fill/stroke, a later matching color rule updating earlier currentColor-derived paint, inline declaration ordering where `color` appears after `fill: currentColor`, presentation `color` feeding `fill="currentColor"`, and selectable SVG text using currentColor-derived fill.
- Isomorphism proof: existing concrete color, opacity, gradient, dash, transform, clip, mask, and text paths keep the same code paths unless the SVG explicitly uses `color` or `currentColor`; CSS specificity/source-order sorting is unchanged; inheritance now carries only the standard `color` property and currentColor flags; floating-point output uses existing color formatting; RNG is not involved.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_current_color_resolves_through_cascade_and_inheritance --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_svg_css_compound_selectors_apply_with_specificity --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_tspan_children_render_as_separate_text_runs --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a common themeable-SVG correctness gap while preserving dependency-free rendering and WASM portability. The active goal remains open because exact repeat/reflect gradients, full soft masks, pattern/image paint servers, richer selector families, and deeper SVG layout semantics remain incomplete.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Descendant And Child CSS Selectors
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T09:51:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`.
- Current profile context: the active profiling handoff remains `tests/artifacts/perf/radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z/`, where `pdf-large` p95 was 323.377 ms over 3 release-perf iterations and the PDF stages still ranked `layout`, `page_content_stream_generation`, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` as the main costs. This pass was a renderer-fidelity change in the hot PDF/SVG output path, not a speed claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 4, confidence 5, effort 2, score 10.0. The real frankenmermaid stylesheet includes selectors such as `.fm-node rect`, `.fm-edge-labeled > rect`, and `marker#arrow-end path`; the renderer already had compound selector parsing and ancestor stacks were cheap to thread through the bounded SVG traversal.
- Root cause: the stylesheet parser intentionally accepted only one compound selector, and style matching only saw the current element. Whitespace or `>` made selectors reject, so real generated SVG rules for grouped nodes, labels, and marker children silently failed instead of cascading.
- Renderer change: replaced the single-part selector with a bounded selector chain supporting simple compound selectors, descendant combinators, and direct-child combinators. The matcher now checks the rightmost part against the current element, walks ancestors right-to-left for descendant/child constraints, and still rejects unsupported sibling, attribute, and pseudo selectors rather than over-applying them. Marker parsing now receives document CSS rules so `marker#id path` can style marker geometry.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_css_compound_selectors_apply_with_specificity` now pins descendant selectors, direct-child selectors, no overmatch outside the group, and no direct-child match through an intermediate group. `pdf_svg_marker_child_css_selectors_style_marker_shapes` pins `marker#id path` styling for marker fills.
- Isomorphism proof: single-part selectors keep the same specificity/source-order sort; unsupported selector families still fail closed; presentation attributes and inline `style` remain later overrides; geometry, transforms, gradients, clipping, masks, opacity, and text paths are unchanged unless a now-supported selector actually matches. Floating-point formatting and PDF resource naming use existing paths; RNG is not involved.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_css_compound_selectors_apply_with_specificity --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_marker_child_css_selectors_style_marker_shapes --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a major real-world stylesheet gap for frankenmermaid-style generated SVG while preserving the dependency-free bounded CSS subset. The active goal remains open because exact repeat/reflect gradients, full soft masks, pattern/image paint servers, richer layout semantics, and broader SVG coverage remain incomplete.

## Active Goal Continuation - Scoped SVG CSS Custom Properties
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T09:58:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-scoped-vars-20260706T0958Z/showcase.pdf`.
- Current profile context: the same `radial-gradient-20260706T090323Z` profile bundle remains the current evidence: PDF rendering is still the dominant scenario, with `pdf-large` p95 323.377 ms and stage evidence showing PDF layout/content-stream/object serialization as the hot path. This pass improves renderer fidelity in that path; it does not claim a speed improvement.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 4, confidence 4, effort 2, score 8.0. frankenmermaid defines many theme values through CSS custom properties scoped to classes such as `.fm-node`, `.fm-node-accent-*`, and edge/label classes. The renderer already had rule matching and `var(...)` resolution, so moving custom properties into the matched cascade was a compact high-value improvement.
- Root cause: custom properties were collected from every stylesheet declaration into one document-wide table before rule matching. That made unrelated class variables able to leak into elements that never matched those selectors, while variables declared on matched ancestors were not modeled as inherited computed state for descendant paints.
- Renderer change: stylesheet rules now retain raw declaration text and parse paint/style patches at application time against an element-specific custom-property table. The table starts with root/svg defaults, then applies variable declarations from each matching ancestor and the current element in specificity/source order, plus inline style custom properties. Root-level variable parsing is limited to root-like selectors so ordinary class-scoped variables no longer become globals.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_css_variables_are_scoped_by_matching_selectors` pins ancestor-scoped variables feeding descendant fills and strokes, sibling scopes retaining independent values, unmatched class variables not leaking over the root fallback, and inline custom properties resolving both inline style paints and presentation `fill="var(...)"` attributes. Existing `pdf_svg_css_variables_resolve_paint_values` continues to pin root-level chains, fallbacks, transparent values, and gradient stop variable resolution.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` with `--pdf-image showcase-mermaid.svg=examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-scoped-vars-20260706T0958Z/showcase.pdf`, copied it to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-scoped-vars-20260706T0958Z/showcase.pdf`, rasterized it with Ghostscript to four PNG pages, and inspected pages 3 and 4. The frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank and readable with boxes, labels, routed arrows, a dashed edge, and the Mermaid source panel intact; the following page still shows visible syntax highlighting.
- Isomorphism proof: SVGs without custom properties still match the same rules and declarations; `:root` variables retain the existing global behavior; CSS specificity/source order remains the tie-breaker; inline and presentation overrides keep their previous relative order; unsupported selector families still fail closed; floating-point output uses existing color/PDF formatting; RNG is not involved.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_css_variables_are_scoped_by_matching_selectors --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_css_variables_resolve_paint_values --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; showcase render plus Ghostscript rasterization and visual inspection.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes a class-variable leakage bug and makes generated SVG theme variables behave more like CSS while keeping the parser bounded, dependency-free, and WASM-safe. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes exact repeat/reflect gradients, full soft masks, pattern/image paint servers, `color-mix(...)`, broader text/layout semantics, and more SVG coverage.

- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T11:22:04Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `examples/showcase-frankenmermaid.toml`, `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/svg-mermaid-shadow-final-20260706T112204Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/svg-mermaid-shadow-final-20260706T112204Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh asset-backed showcase render used the release-perf `fmd` binary and completed in 0.02 s wall time with 8,352 KB max RSS, producing a 59,882-byte PDF. The output artifact is `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/svg-mermaid-shadow-final-20260706T112204Z/showcase.pdf`.
- Root cause: SVG filter support collapsed every `filter` value to a boolean shadow flag. That made real generated SVG shadow parameters from `feDropShadow` and stylesheet `drop-shadow(...)` disappear: offsets, flood color, RGBA alpha, and paint opacity composition all fell back to a fixed opaque gray `2,2` vector duplicate.
- Renderer change: added a compact `SvgShadow` value, parsed bounded `<filter><feDropShadow .../></filter>` definitions, parsed the common CSS `drop-shadow(x y blur rgba(...))` form, threaded resolved filter definitions through the existing SVG style cascade, and emitted PDF vector shadow fallbacks using the resolved offset, color, and composed fill/stroke alpha. Unsupported or unresolved URL filters still use the previous deterministic fallback instead of disappearing.
- Showcase change: tightened the frankenmermaid showcase config to `theme = "corporate"`, `node_spacing = 56`, `rank_spacing = 88`, and `rounded_corners = 8`, then regenerated `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` from `/dp/frankenmermaid`.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_filter_drop_shadow_gets_vector_shadow_fallback` pins `feDropShadow dx/dy`, flood color, and flood opacity. `pdf_svg_css_drop_shadow_uses_declared_shadow_values` pins CSS `drop-shadow(...)` offsets, RGBA color alpha, and composition with `fill-opacity`.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` with `--pdf-image showcase-mermaid.svg=examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, rasterized with Ghostscript, and inspected `showcase-page-03.png`. The frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank, labels are readable, colored strokes and the dashed SVG edge survive, and the adjacent Mermaid/source content remains legible.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; focused PDF shadow tests; `git diff --check`; release-perf showcase render and Ghostscript rasterization.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a concrete generated-SVG fidelity bug without adding dependencies or widening the renderer beyond a bounded native-PDF fallback. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes soft-filter blur, full soft masks, exact repeat/reflect gradients, pattern/image paint servers, and broader layout/text semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - Same-Run Segment Width Optimization
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T11:32:46Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260706T1126Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-segbuilder-proof-20260706T1132Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-same-run-width-proof-20260706T1136Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-same-run-width-after-20260706T1140Z/`.

PDF stage evidence ranked `layout` first at 244.030 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 40.838 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.069 ms p95.
- Rejected trial: a broader `build_segs_adjusted` rewrite deferred all segment shaping until segment finalization. It removed more work, but the golden byte proof caught different `pdf-large.pdf` bytes (609,420 B vs the baseline 609,524 B), likely due to slightly different accumulated floating-point x-position rounding. That trial was rejected.
- Accepted renderer/layout optimization: kept the original segment width accumulation order but moved the per-token `token_width` call out of the same-run append arm where its result was immediately overwritten. Same-slot/same-link/same-strike token appends now do one shaping call for the growing segment instead of also shaping the individual token first.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. The profile identifies PDF layout as dominant, and source tracing showed redundant shaping in a layout hot path. The accepted lever is intentionally narrow because byte-identical output is more important than a larger speculative rewrite.
- Isomorphism proof: ordering and run grouping are unchanged; tie-breaking is unchanged; the x-position accumulation order and shaped segment-width updates are unchanged; floating-point output stays byte-identical for rendered artifacts; RNG is not involved. The only removed work was a shaped width whose value was not read on same-run appends.
- Behavior proof: `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-same-run-width-proof-20260706T1136Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf` has the same SHA-256 as the baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260706T1126Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf` (`11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`). Output artifacts for HTML, parser HTML, PDF showcase, compression lengths, font subset, hyphenation points, and paragraph breaks also compare byte-identical; timing JSON differs as expected.
- Directional performance: focused post-change run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-same-run-width-after-20260706T1140Z/` reported `pdf-large` p50 308.948 ms and p95 321.448 ms over 5 iterations, with the layout stage at 236.392 ms p95. Compared with the fresh 3-iteration baseline layout p95 of 244.030 ms, the specific layout-stage evidence supports the change, while end-to-end p95 remains within normal short-run variance.
- Verification so far: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-profile-20260706T1126Z`; `sha256sum -c` from the baseline golden directory; focused PDF profile proof test; `cargo fmt --check`; rendered-output byte comparisons; `cargo check --all-targets`; focused release-perf `pdf-large` reprofile.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a small but real profile-driven cleanup in the dominant PDF layout path. The active goal remains open because broader PDF/SVG rendering quality and performance work remains.
