## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Stroke Miter Limit Fidelity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T11:53:06Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the latest profile handoff remains `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260706T1126Z/`, where `pdf-large` ranked first at 319.524 ms p95 and PDF stages ranked `layout` at 244.030 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 40.838 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.069 ms p95. This pass is an SVG/PDF renderer-fidelity step in the hot PDF writer surface, not a speed claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. `stroke-miterlimit` is common in exported icon/diagram SVGs and directly affects corner rendering for miter joins. The renderer already supported line cap, line join, dash arrays, inheritance, CSS patches, and PDF stroke operators, so this was a compact high-confidence fidelity improvement.
- Root cause: `SvgStyle` tracked stroke width, cap, join, and dash state, but ignored `stroke-miterlimit` everywhere. SVGs that explicitly constrained miter joins therefore rendered with PDF's current/default miter behavior instead of their declared vector geometry.
- Renderer change: added optional inherited `miter_limit` state to `SvgStyle`, parsed `stroke-miterlimit` from presentation attributes, stylesheet declarations, and inline `style` declarations, preserved the value through CSS patch application and line/polyline inherited-style construction, and emitted the PDF `M` operator from `append_svg_stroke_options` when an explicit finite value of at least `1.0` is declared.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_css_class_stroke_styles_apply_to_vector_shapes` now pins both presentation-attribute `stroke-miterlimit="3"` and stylesheet `stroke-miterlimit: 2.5`, including exact PDF operator order (`w`, `J`, `j`, `M`, dash, path, stroke) for explicit miter joins.
- Isomorphism proof: SVGs without explicit `stroke-miterlimit` keep the prior output because the new style field defaults to `None` and no `M` operator is emitted. Existing cap/join/dash parsing and source-order cascade are unchanged; invalid values below `1.0` fail closed and inherit the previous computed value; floating-point output uses existing `pdf_num`; RNG is not involved.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_css_class_stroke_styles_apply_to_vector_shapes --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `git diff --check`; `cargo test --quiet`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes another real SVG stroke-style gap while keeping the renderer dependency-free and preserving current output for SVGs that do not request a miter limit. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes exact repeat/reflect gradients, full soft masks/filters, pattern/image paint servers, and broader layout/text semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - Native Linear Repeat/Reflect Gradients
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T12:04:02Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the current performance handoff remains `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260706T1126Z/`, where `pdf-large` ranked first at 319.524 ms p95 and PDF stages ranked `layout` at 244.030 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 40.838 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.069 ms p95. This pass improves the SVG/PDF rendering surface within that hot output path; it is not claimed as an end-to-end speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 4, effort 2, score 6.0. The ledger repeatedly identified exact repeat/reflect gradients as remaining world-class SVG work, and the renderer already had native axial shadings, gradient transforms, shape clipping, and PDF resource registration. That made bounded linear spread rendering a high-leverage one-lever improvement.
- Root cause: the native gradient parser rejected any non-`pad` `spreadMethod`, so `spreadMethod="repeat"` and `spreadMethod="reflect"` fell back to a representative solid color. That avoided wrong pad semantics but visibly lost repeated/ reflected gradient bands in icons, diagrams, and theme assets.
- Renderer change: added explicit gradient spread state, explicit PDF shading `/Extend` flags, and a bounded linear spread resolver. For `repeat` and `reflect`, the resolver projects the target shape bbox onto the gradient axis, computes the finite set of period bands needed under the existing shape clip, emits one non-extended native axial shading per band, and alternates stop order for odd `reflect` periods. If a pathological gradient would require more than 64 bands or exceed the page shading resource cap, the renderer falls back to the existing representative color instead of emitting a huge or partial PDF.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_linear_gradient_transform_and_spread_method_are_respected` now pins transformed pad gradients, two-band `repeat` output using `/Extend [false false]`, two-band `reflect` output with reversed odd-period stop colors, and all period bands painted under one clipped shape path.
- Fresh-eyes fix: after the first implementation pass, review found that page-resource exhaustion could otherwise register only part of a multi-band gradient. Added an all-or-fallback `pdf_shadings_fit` preflight so repeated gradients never render partially when the 256-shading cap is near exhaustion.
- Isomorphism proof: default/pad gradients keep the previous single native shading and `/Extend [true true]`; unsupported or too-large spread cases keep the prior solid representative fallback; non-gradient fills, strokes, transforms, clipping, masks, opacity, text, and image paths are unchanged; floating-point formatting uses existing `pdf_num`/`pdf_fixed3`; RNG is not involved.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_linear_gradient_transform_and_spread_method_are_respected --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test --quiet`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes a concrete solid-color fallback for common linear SVG spread methods while staying dependency-free, PDF-native, and bounded. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes exact radial spread methods, soft filters/masks, pattern/image paint servers, and deeper layout/text semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - Native Radial Repeat/Reflect Gradient Rings
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T12:35:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-radial-spread-profile-20260706T1228Z/`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/radial-spread-20260706T1235Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh measurement bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-radial-spread-profile-20260706T1228Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` first at 313.263 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. Stage attribution remains dominated by PDF layout at 239.408 ms p95, page content stream generation at 41.425 ms p95, and PDF object serialization at 24.943 ms p95. This pass is renderer-fidelity work inside the hot PDF/SVG surface, not an end-to-end speed claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 4, effort 2, score 6.0. The previous pass added exact bounded repeat/reflect support for linear gradients, while radial gradients still rejected every non-`pad` spread method. The existing native PDF type-3 radial shading path and all-or-fallback shading-resource preflight made concentric radial rings a compact, high-confidence extension.
- Root cause: `resolve_svg_radial_gradient` returned a single `PdfShading` only for `spreadMethod="pad"` and returned `None` for `repeat`/`reflect`. That sent supported circular radial gradients through the representative solid-color fallback even when PDF can paint finite concentric rings exactly under the shape clip.
- Renderer change: changed radial gradient resolution to return `Vec<PdfShading>` like the linear path, preserving the old single extended type-3 shading for `pad`. Added a bounded repeat/reflect resolver for the exact concentric circular subset (`fr=0`, focal center equals outer center). It computes the finite rings needed to cover the target shape bbox, emits non-extended native radial shadings for each ring, reverses stop order on odd `reflect` rings, caps output at 64 rings, and falls back to the existing representative color for non-concentric, focal-circle, too-large, or non-finite cases.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_radial_gradient_repeat_and_reflect_emit_bounded_native_rings` pins first and second native radial ring coordinates, `/Extend [false false]`, forward `repeat` stop order, reversed odd `reflect` stop order, and the clipped multi-ring paint sequence for both shapes. Existing `pdf_svg_radial_gradients_use_native_pdf_shading_when_circular` pins unchanged pad behavior and non-circular fallback behavior.
- Isomorphism proof: default/pad radial gradients still emit the same single extended type-3 shading; unsupported repeat/reflect radial cases keep the previous representative-color fallback; non-gradient fills, strokes, transforms, clipping, masks, opacity, text, patterns, and linear gradients are unchanged; large canonical PDF output stayed byte-identical to the prior profile artifact (`11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`); floating-point output uses existing `pdf_num`/`pdf_fixed3`; RNG is not involved.
- frankenmermaid proof: `/dp/frankenmermaid` regenerated `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` from `examples/showcase-mermaid.mmd` using `examples/showcase-frankenmermaid.toml`, then current `fmd` rendered `examples/showcase.md` with `--pdf-image showcase-mermaid.svg=examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/radial-spread-20260706T1235Z/showcase.pdf` (59,886 bytes). Ghostscript rasterized all four pages, and visual inspection confirmed the diagram page is nonblank and readable with boxes, routed arrows, arrowheads, a dashed edge, and readable Mermaid source; the code page still shows visible Rust, Python, JSON, and shell syntax highlighting.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_radial_gradient_repeat_and_reflect_emit_bounded_native_rings --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_radial_gradients_use_native_pdf_shading_when_circular --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-radial-spread-profile-20260706T1228Z`; frankenmermaid regeneration; showcase PDF render; Ghostscript rasterization; visual inspection of pages 3 and 4.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes the remaining exact radial repeat/reflect gap for the common concentric circular case while staying dependency-free, bounded, PDF-native, and WASM-safe. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, broader radial spread geometries, image paint servers, and deeper SVG text/layout semantics.

## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG Text Font Slot Fidelity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T12:45:59Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review surface: peer-authored SVG/PDF renderer work, with artifact-script safety and generated frankenmermaid SVGs checked as context. The artifact run-id scripts already source the shared validator before constructing artifact paths; the concrete renderer defect found was in SVG text style fidelity.
- Root cause: SVG text parsing threaded fill, opacity, clipping, masks, transforms, font size, and text anchoring through the PDF text path, but it discarded `font-weight` and `font-style`. As a result, frankenmermaid-generated SVG labels that declare `font-weight: 600/700`, `font-weight="bold"`, or `font-style="italic"` rendered with the regular `/F1` body face. The subsetting pass also assumed all SVG text used `F_BODY`, so simply changing the emitter would have risked referencing a font resource that was not embedded.
- Renderer change: added inherited SVG text weight/slant state to `SvgStyle`, parsed `font-weight` and `font-style` from presentation attributes, stylesheet rules, inline styles, and CSS variables, mapped numeric weights `600+` and `bold`/`bolder` to existing bold slots, mapped `italic`/`oblique` to existing italic slots, stored the resolved slot on each `SvgText`, and made font discovery/subsetting/shaping/width calculation/PDF text emission all use that same slot.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_text_font_weight_and_style_select_embedded_font_slots` pins stylesheet class, CSS-variable, numeric-weight, italic, oblique, combined bold-italic, and medium-weight fallback behavior. `pdf_svg_tspan_inherits_and_overrides_font_weight_and_style` pins inherited parent bold+italic styling and an inline `tspan` override that keeps bold while returning to upright style.
- First-principles proof: the visible PDF text operator, shaped glyph stream, anchor width calculation, subset seed glyphs, and embedded font resource are now derived from one slot value. SVGs without declared weight/slant keep the previous regular face because the new style defaults are normal/upright. Numeric 500 stays regular because the bundled font set does not include a medium face.
- Verification so far: `cargo fmt --check`; focused new PDF tests; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; UBS was run but produced broad pre-existing JS/Rust pattern counts without actionable locations in the captured output, so it was treated as scanner noise rather than a convergence gate.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a real frankenmermaid/SVG text fidelity defect without adding dependencies or broadening the renderer. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, image paint servers, richer CSS text sizing/letter-spacing, and deeper text layout semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Dominant Baseline Text Placement
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T12:57:55Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the fresh handoff bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-textstyle-profile-20260706T1250Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` first at 311.721 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. PDF stage attribution is still dominated by `layout` at 237.438 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 40.298 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.034 ms p95. This pass is a renderer-fidelity correction in the hot PDF/SVG surface, not an end-to-end speed claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. `/dp/frankenmermaid` emits `dominant-baseline` values for generated diagram labels, and the existing SVG text path already had inherited style, transforms, selectable PDF text, tspan overrides, and font slot selection. That made baseline placement a small, high-confidence fidelity fix with little risk to non-SVG output.
- Root cause: SVG text parsing ignored `dominant-baseline` and `alignment-baseline`, so labels generated with `middle` or `central` baseline semantics were emitted as if the `x/y` coordinate were an alphabetic baseline. In PDF output, that makes vertically centered diagram labels sit too low/high relative to their boxes even though shapes, transforms, clips, masks, and font slots are otherwise honored.
- Renderer change: added inherited `SvgDominantBaseline` state to `SvgStyle`, parsed `dominant-baseline` and `alignment-baseline` from presentation attributes, stylesheet rules, inline styles, and CSS variables, preserved the value through group and tspan inheritance, stored it on each `SvgText`, and applied a deterministic local-y baseline offset before converting SVG text coordinates into the PDF selectable text matrix.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_dominant_baseline_adjusts_selectable_text_position` pins default alphabetic behavior, direct `dominant-baseline="central"`, stylesheet `dominant-baseline: var(...)`, and a `tspan` inline override back to `auto`. The test compares emitted PDF text matrix y positions rather than only checking style parsing, so it proves the placement path changed.
- First-principles proof: SVGs without an explicit baseline keep byte-for-byte text placement semantics because the new state defaults to `Auto` and has a zero offset. Baseline offsets are applied in local SVG coordinates before the existing transform conversion, so rotated or translated labels move along the same local text axis rather than page y only. No dependencies, filesystem assumptions, or CLI-only behavior were added.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_dominant_baseline_adjusts_selectable_text_position --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a concrete generated-SVG text-placement bug while preserving the dependency-free, selectable-text PDF renderer. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes letter-spacing/TJ placement, soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, image paint servers, and deeper text layout semantics.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Letter Spacing Text Placement
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T13:08:14Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-letter-spacing-profile-20260706T1300Z/`.
- Current profile context: fresh measurement bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-letter-spacing-profile-20260706T1300Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 320.160 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. PDF stage attribution remains dominated by `layout` at 244.307 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 42.468 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.930 ms p95. The large PDF golden checksum stayed `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The current frankenmermaid showcase SVG and `/dp/frankenmermaid` themes emit `letter-spacing: -0.02em`, `-0.01em`, and `0.01em` for diagram labels. The PDF SVG text path already handled style cascade, CSS variables, font slots, baselines, transforms, tspan splitting, and selectable text, so this was a compact high-confidence renderer-fidelity step.
- Root cause: SVG text parsing ignored `letter-spacing`, so frankenmermaid labels rendered with default font advances even when the SVG requested tighter or looser tracking. The anchor-width calculation also used untracked text width, so centered labels could be placed as if their visual width had not changed.
- Renderer change: added inherited `SvgTextSpacing` state to `SvgStyle`, parsed `letter-spacing` from presentation attributes, stylesheet rules, inline styles, `normal`, `em`/`ex`/`%`/numeric units, and CSS variables, preserved it through group and tspan inheritance, stored resolved point spacing on each `SvgText`, included spacing in SVG text/tspan advance estimates, included spacing in PDF text-anchor width math, and emitted the spacing through PDF `TJ` adjustments so text remains selectable and ToUnicode-backed instead of rasterized.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_letter_spacing_adjusts_selectable_text_and_anchor_width` pins stylesheet `letter-spacing: var(...)`, direct negative `letter-spacing="-0.05em"`, centered-anchor width movement, positive spacing as negative PDF `TJ` adjustment, negative spacing as positive PDF `TJ` adjustment, and a `tspan` inline reset back to `normal`.
- First-principles proof: SVGs without explicit letter spacing keep the previous output path because the new style defaults to zero and the existing `kerned_tj` wrapper still passes a zero spacing adjustment for all non-SVG text. The adjustment is applied in PDF text-space units after the same shaping/kerning pass, so glyph selection, ToUnicode maps, font subsetting, color, opacity, clipping, masks, transforms, and selectable text semantics are preserved. No dependency, CLI-only behavior, filesystem assumption, or WASM-incompatible feature was added.
- Verification: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-letter-spacing-profile-20260706T1300Z`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_letter_spacing_adjusts_selectable_text_and_anchor_width --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete frankenmermaid-generated SVG text-spacing gap while keeping the renderer dependency-free, selectable, deterministic, and WASM-safe. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, image paint servers, broader text layout semantics, and deeper low-level performance opportunities in PDF layout/page-stream generation.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Embedded PNG Image Paint Support
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T13:26:20Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-embedded-image-profile-20260706T1325Z/`.
- Current profile context: post-change measurement bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-embedded-image-profile-20260706T1325Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 311.113 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. PDF stage attribution remains dominated by `layout` at 238.794 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.698 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.274 ms p95. `image_asset_collection` stayed negligible at 3.256 us p95 for the large corpus, and the large PDF golden checksum stayed `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. The SVG/PDF path already handled vector shapes, gradients, patterns, markers, text, clipping, masks, opacity, and embedded top-level PNG assets, but it had no `SvgElement::Image` representation. SVG diagrams produced by real tools can embed small raster icons, logos, screenshots, or texture chips as `data:image/png;base64,...`; dropping those nodes is a visible correctness failure in the exact dependency-free renderer surface the project is trying to make world-class.
- Root cause: `parse_svg_document` and reusable `<use>` expansion enumerated only vector geometry and text nodes. Because nested `<image>` tags were not parsed into the SVG element list, they never reached image resource collection, page resource emission, or content-stream drawing. The omission was silent: the surrounding SVG still rendered, so diagrams looked mostly correct while losing embedded raster content.
- Renderer change: added `SvgEmbeddedImage` and `SvgElement::Image`, parsed direct and reusable SVG `<image>` nodes, restricted support to bounded embedded PNG data URIs only, decoded base64 with a small dependency-free decoder, reused the existing PNG parser/decoder and PDF image XObject writer, keyed inline PNGs deterministically with a stable FNV-1a digest plus byte length, recursively collected nested raster resources from vector SVGs, and drew them in SVG user coordinates with the vertical flip needed to keep the raster upright under the existing SVG y-down transform. CSS/presentation visibility, transforms, clips, hard masks, and image `opacity` are honored; hidden images return before base64 decode so invisible data payloads do not consume decoder work. External URLs, filesystem references, recursive SVG-in-SVG images, and non-PNG data URIs remain unsupported by design.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_embedded_png_image_renders_as_nested_xobject` pins a supplied SVG asset containing a base64 PNG `<image>`. The test asserts allocation of a real `/Subtype /Image` XObject, page `/XObject` resource exposure, the exact nested image drawing matrix `10 0 0 -8 4 13 cm /Im1 Do`, PDF ExtGState opacity `/GSa05000500 gs`, and preservation of the outer SVG figure alt text. The existing pure-SVG test still asserts no image XObject for SVGs without embedded rasters.
- First-principles proof: top-level PNGs still use the existing image path, pure SVGs without `<image>` still allocate no XObjects, and nested PNGs now share the same bounded PNG validation, alpha-mask handling, deterministic object ordering, and PDF resource naming as ordinary Markdown images. The implementation introduces no third-party dependency, no filesystem/network access, no unsafe, no async/runtime assumption, and no WASM-incompatible API. The data URI decoder rejects malformed padding, non-base64 payloads, non-PNG media types, and payloads whose decoded byte count would exceed the existing compressed-image ceiling before invoking PNG parsing.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_embedded_png_image_renders_as_nested_xobject --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-embedded-image-profile-20260706T1325Z`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a concrete diagram-fidelity hole in the dependency-free SVG renderer while preserving current performance shape and the existing large-corpus PDF bytes. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, broader image paint-server behavior, external-resource policy decisions, and deeper low-level performance work in PDF layout/page-stream generation.

## Active Goal Continuation - Inline Code Chip Width Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T13:33:26Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-chip-width-profile-20260706T1332Z/`.
- Current profile context: the prior post-change profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-embedded-image-profile-20260706T1325Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 311.113 ms p95, with `layout` at 238.794 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.698 ms p95, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.274 ms p95. The new short-run bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-chip-width-profile-20260706T1332Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` first at 323.465 ms p95, with the same dominant stage ordering; this is within short-run variance and is not claimed as an end-to-end speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Page-content generation draws inline-code chip backgrounds for monospace inline spans. Each `Seg` already carries the shaped layout advance used for following segment placement, strikethrough, link annotation geometry, and prior same-run width proofs, but the chip pass re-shaped the same monospace text just to compute the background's right edge.
- Root cause: the chip-decoration path treated width as a local rendering concern and called `text_width(&seg.text, size, F_MONO, faces)` even though layout had already measured that exact segment. That duplicated shaping work in `page_content_stream_generation` and could diverge subtly from the authoritative segment advance when a segment width reflects cross-token shaping or previous layout decisions.
- Renderer change: inline-code chip backgrounds now use `seg.width` directly for the right edge. The left edge, vertical bounds, padding, radius, colors, text drawing, tagged structure, annotations, and all non-chip content are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: the large benchmark PDF remains byte-identical to the previous post-change profile artifact: `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-chip-width-profile-20260706T1332Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf` and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-embedded-image-profile-20260706T1325Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf` both have SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. The small showcase PDF changed by 14 bytes because two decorative inline-code chip rounded rectangles moved to the stored shaped width; a decompressed stream diff showed only those two `/Artifact` rectangle coordinate lines changed, with no text, annotation, structure, or image content changes.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_code_blocks`; `cargo test --test pdf_test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-chip-width-profile-20260706T1332Z`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE but low-amplitude; this removes redundant PDF page-content width measurement and makes chip background geometry use the same shaped segment width as the rest of the renderer. The active goal remains open because the meaningful remaining performance work is still in broader PDF layout/page-stream generation, and full world-class SVG still includes soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, and more SVG coverage.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Root Viewport Aspect Mapping
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T13:48:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-aspect-profile-20260706T1345Z/`.
- Current profile context: fresh measurement bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-aspect-profile-20260706T1345Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 310.202 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. PDF stage attribution remains dominated by `layout` at 232.125 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.046 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.921 ms p95. The large benchmark PDF stayed byte-identical to the prior profile artifact with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. The SVG renderer already handled shapes, text, gradients, markers, clips, masks, and embedded PNGs, but its root geometry collapsed the SVG viewport and viewBox into one rectangle. Real diagram generators often emit `width`/`height` plus a different `viewBox`, and SVG's default `preserveAspectRatio="xMidYMid meet"` is essential for avoiding stretched diagrams.
- Root cause: `parse_svg_image_asset` used `viewBox` dimensions as the intrinsic PDF image dimensions even when the root SVG declared an explicit viewport, and `draw_svg_image` independently scaled x/y from the viewBox to the rendered image box. That made explicit wide/tall SVG viewports either disappear or stretch content non-uniformly, and selectable SVG text had its own duplicated coordinate formula that could drift from the vector shape transform.
- Renderer change: added root `SvgViewport` and `SvgPreserveAspectRatio` state to `PdfSvgImage`, parse root `width`/`height` separately from `viewBox`, default to `xMidYMid meet`, support `preserveAspectRatio="none"` and `meet`/`slice` alignments, and compute one `SvgImageTransform` shared by vector shape CTMs, selectable SVG text matrices, and SVG text clip/mask geometry. Percentage root dimensions are treated as unresolved intrinsic sizes and fall back to the viewBox instead of being misread as literal `100` units.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_root_viewport_preserves_viewbox_aspect_ratio` pins a 200-by-100 viewport with a square viewBox: the PDF figure becomes 150pt wide, the vector CTM uses uniform 0.75 scale with a 37.5pt x offset, and selectable text uses the same centered transform. `pdf_svg_preserve_aspect_ratio_none_allows_non_uniform_viewport_scale` pins the explicit stretch path. `pdf_svg_percentage_root_viewport_falls_back_to_viewbox_size` prevents responsive `width="100%" height="100%"` SVGs from shrinking to a fake 100-by-100 viewport.
- First-principles proof: SVGs without explicit root dimensions keep viewBox-derived intrinsic size; SVGs with only `width`/`height` still get an equivalent zero-origin viewBox; responsive percentage SVGs preserve the previous viewBox-based sizing; no filesystem, network, native runtime, unsafe, dependency, or async behavior was added. The shared transform removes duplicated coordinate math for shapes versus selectable text rather than adding another special case.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_root_viewport --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_preserve_aspect_ratio_none --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_percentage_root_viewport --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-aspect-profile-20260706T1345Z`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this fixes a concrete SVG viewport/aspect-ratio correctness gap while keeping large-corpus output byte-identical and preserving the dependency-free, selectable-text PDF renderer. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes soft blur/filter semantics, full SVG soft masks, stroke gradient geometry, broader image paint-server behavior, and deeper layout/page-stream optimization.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Paragraph Break Scratch Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T13:55:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-scratch-profile-20260706T1351Z/`.
- Current profile context: the prior bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-aspect-profile-20260706T1345Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 310.202 ms p95, with PDF `layout` dominant at 232.125 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.046 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.921 ms p95. The new bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-scratch-profile-20260706T1351Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` first at 317.174 ms p95 and layout first at 239.696 ms p95; this is short-run variance, not a speed win claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The profile recommendation called out layout scratch reuse, and the line-breaking crate already exposed `break_paragraph_into` plus `ParagraphLayoutScratch` specifically for caller-owned reuse. The PDF path was still using the allocating `break_paragraph` wrapper for every normal and list-prefixed paragraph.
- Root cause: `layout_inlines` and `layout_prefixed_inlines` built paragraph items and then called `break_paragraph(&built.items, content_w)`, which allocated a fresh `ParagraphLayoutScratch` and fresh `Vec<LineBreak>` for each paragraph. That duplicated setup work in the dominant layout stage even though all paragraph breaks happen serially inside one render call.
- Renderer change: `LayoutCx` now owns a render-call-local `ParagraphLayoutScratch` and `Vec<LineBreak>`, and the PDF inline layout paths call `break_paragraph_into` through that context. The chosen line breaks are copied out as `LineBreak` values during emission, preserving the existing output logic while retaining scratch/output capacity across paragraphs.
- Regression/proof target: existing render-tree goldens and profiled PDF byte tests cover normal paragraphs, lists, tables, hyphenation, pagination, and structure output. The fresh profile artifact's `profiled_bytes_equal_normal_pdf` obligation passed, and the large benchmark PDF remained byte-identical to the previous profile artifact with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- First-principles proof: ordering and tie-breaking are unchanged because `break_paragraph_into` is the implementation called by the old wrapper; only ownership/lifetime of scratch and output buffers moved from per-call locals into the per-render layout context. Floating-point behavior, hyphenation cache keys, line-break demerits, greedy fallback, tagged PDF structure, and PDF serialization are unchanged. No dependency, unsafe code, native runtime assumption, filesystem access, or WASM-incompatible behavior was added.
- Verification: `cargo test render_tree --lib`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_table --test pdf_test`; `cargo test pdf_reuses_hyphenation_cache_for_repeated_words --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_uses_discretionary_hyphen_only_for_chosen_hyphen_breaks --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-layout-scratch-profile-20260706T1351Z`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE but low-amplitude; this removes avoidable per-paragraph line-break scratch allocations in the dominant PDF layout path while keeping output byte-identical. The active goal remains open because the next higher-leverage work likely sits in paragraph item/token construction, parser block classification, or deeper SVG features rather than this single scratch lever.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Plain Inline Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T14:08:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-inline-fastpath-profile-20260706T140548Z/`.
- Current profile context: the prior parser-focused bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-fastpath-profile-20260706T140059Z/` still had `parser-large` at 37.396 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations, with `inline_parse` totaling 66.782 ms and synthetic inline allocation count 2,322,282 across the three profiled parses. The final bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-inline-fastpath-profile-20260706T140548Z/` drops `parser-large` to 29.053 ms p95, `block_parse_total` to 24.694 ms p95, `inline_parse` total to 43.831 ms, and synthetic inline allocation count to 1,614,315. The generated HTML golden checksum stayed `989843fa34b8668fb2798df50cfe7f72659be5a9c89a0ffcbd83b094fb5f8064`, and the large PDF checksum stayed `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 4, confidence 5, effort 1, score 20.0. Stage attribution showed parser work dominated by block/paragraph/inline parsing. The inline parser was paying for `Vec<char>`, delimiter tokenization, and emphasis resolution even for plain table cells, headings, and paragraphs that contain no inline syntax.
- Root cause: `parse_inlines_with_refs_profiled` unconditionally collected every inline run into `Vec<char>` and entered the full tokenizer/resolver. This made common plain text pay the same setup cost as text containing links, code spans, entities, hard breaks, emphasis, raw HTML, bare emails, or GFM bare URLs.
- Parser change: added a conservative byte scanner before the full inline parser. Runs with no inline trigger bytes and no `http://`, `https://`, `www.`, or `@` return a single `Inline::Text` directly while still recording the `inline_parse` profile stage. The scanner deliberately punts to the full parser for every syntax-triggering byte (`\`, newline, backtick, `!`, `[`, `<`, `&`, `~`, `*`, `_`, `@`) and for GFM bare URL prefixes, so autolinks and all existing inline syntax keep the old parser path.
- Reference-collection cleanup: added a no-reference-candidate bypass for sources without `]:`, and a plain-line fast path inside top-level/nested reference collection so ordinary lines without parser-significant bytes do not run the full conservative line scanner. The generated large fixture still contains repeated `[home]: ...` definitions, so this part is correctness/ergonomics cleanup rather than the main speed win.
- Regression target: `profiled_parser_reference_collection_skips_work_when_no_definition_candidate_exists` pins the no-`]:` reference path with zero reference-stage allocations. `profiled_parser_plain_inline_fast_path_skips_tokenizer_without_losing_autolinks` pins the single-text inline result/profile accounting and proves `www.example.org` still takes the full parser path and autolinks.
- First-principles proof: the fast inline path is a strict subset of previous `Inline::Text` outcomes. Any byte that can start an inline construct, escape, entity, HTML/autolink, strikethrough/emphasis delimiter, image/link, soft/hard break, bare email, or bare URL forces the original parser. No dependency, unsafe code, filesystem access, native runtime assumption, or WASM-incompatible behavior was added.
- Verification: `cargo test profiled_parser_plain_inline_fast_path_skips_tokenizer_without_losing_autolinks --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_parser_reference_collection_skips_work_when_no_definition_candidate_exists --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test gfm_bare_urls_autolink_with_punctuation_outside --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test refdef_paragraph_tests --lib`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs tests/parser_conformance.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-parser-inline-fastpath-profile-20260706T140548Z`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a real parser hot-path win with behavior pinned by parser conformance tests and golden artifact checks. The active goal remains open because the current recommendation still points at block/reference/classification work, and broader PDF/SVG renderer work remains unfinished.

## Active Goal Continuation - File-Input Auto SVG/PNG Assets
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T14:34:01Z.
- Files changed: `src/cli.rs`, `tests/cli_contract.rs`, `README.md`, `examples/showcase.md`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-live-baseline-20260706T1424Z/`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/auto-local-20260706T1430Z/`.
- Current profile context: fresh `release-perf` harness run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-live-baseline-20260706T1424Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 304.354 ms p95 over 3 iterations. Stage attribution still puts PDF `layout` first at 230.605 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 41.265 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.941 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 270.642 us p95 per stream. Parser work is much lower after the prior fast path: `parser-large` is 27.408 ms p95.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 4, confidence 5, effort 2, score 10.0. The showcase already contained a frankenmermaid-generated SVG and the PDF renderer already drew host-supplied SVG bytes as vector content. The weak point was the native CLI integration: the first-try command `fmd examples/showcase.md --to pdf --out ...` did not supply the sibling SVG bytes unless the caller remembered a manual `--pdf-image` mapping.
- Root cause: the render core correctly stayed filesystem-free and accepted explicit `PdfImageAsset` bytes, but the CLI only populated that asset list from explicit `--pdf-image` flags. File-input Markdown documents with relative local `.png`/`.svg` image destinations therefore fell back to visible alt text even when the referenced file sat beside the Markdown source. That made the frankenmermaid showcase integration fragile and contradicted the product goal that ordinary Markdown files including SVGs should render well to PDF.
- CLI change: for file-input PDF renders only, the native CLI now parses the Markdown AST once, collects image destinations structurally, and auto-loads existing relative local `.png`/`.svg` destinations from the Markdown file's directory. Explicit `--pdf-image DEST=PATH` assets are still loaded first and keep first-match precedence. Auto-loading is deliberately disabled for `--text`, stdin, absolute paths, URI schemes, backslash paths, parent-directory traversal, non-PNG/SVG extensions, missing files, and directories. Found auto assets share the existing `--max-pdf-image-bytes` cap and input-error preflight. The library/WASM render core remains host-supplied-bytes only and performs no filesystem or network access.
- Regression targets: `pdf_render_auto_loads_relative_svg_assets_for_file_inputs` proves the real `fmd` binary renders a file-relative SVG as vector figure content without a warning or manual mapping. `pdf_render_does_not_auto_load_assets_for_raw_text_inputs` proves raw text does not implicitly read the current directory and still warns with the explicit mapping guidance. `pdf_render_auto_loaded_assets_obey_the_pdf_image_byte_limit` proves found local assets are capped before output is written.
- frankenmermaid proof: `/dp/frankenmermaid` regenerated `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/auto-local-20260706T1430Z/showcase-mermaid.svg` from `examples/showcase-mermaid.mmd` using `examples/showcase-frankenmermaid.toml`; it is byte-identical to `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` (`4cc1097e4435f27730e580a21d3c00140dfc0c0799881b8217cd449321aaf0b9`). Current `fmd` then rendered `examples/showcase.md --to pdf` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/auto-local-20260706T1430Z/showcase-auto.pdf` without any `--pdf-image` flag and without warnings. Ghostscript rasterized the PDF via `/tmp` to page PNGs; visual inspection of `page-03.png` showed the generated SVG rendered as nonblank vector diagram content with readable labels, colored boxes/strokes, arrowheads, a dashed edge, and the Mermaid source block below it.
- First-principles proof: output semantics for explicit mappings are preserved because explicit assets are inserted before auto assets and the PDF resolver keeps the first matching destination. Non-file inputs cannot gain surprising filesystem reads because auto-loading requires a real Markdown file base directory. Remote/data/absolute/traversing destinations remain unresolved unless the caller explicitly supplies bytes. Existing PDF image decode and SVG rendering policy is unchanged; the CLI only resolves bytes earlier. No dependency, unsafe code, network access, core filesystem access, or WASM-incompatible behavior was added.
- Verification: `cargo run --profile release-perf --example fmd_perf_harness -- --scenario all --iters 3 --out-dir tests/artifacts/perf/continue-live-baseline-20260706T1424Z/golden`; frankenmermaid regeneration command with `--config examples/showcase-frankenmermaid.toml`; byte comparison of generated showcase SVG; `cargo run --bin fmd -- examples/showcase.md --to pdf --out tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/auto-local-20260706T1430Z/showcase-auto.pdf --json`; Ghostscript rasterization and visual inspection; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo build --no-default-features`; `cargo test --test cli_contract -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this makes the frankenmermaid showcase path real for the first-try file-input PDF workflow while preserving the core architecture boundary. The active goal remains open because further world-class SVG work still includes deeper soft-filter/mask coverage, broader paint-server behavior, more SVG text/layout semantics, and ongoing low-level PDF layout/page-generation optimization.

## Active Goal Continuation - Native SVG Line Gradient Strokes
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T14:58:11Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/stroke-gradient-line-20260706T145422Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-stroke-gradient-line-profile-20260706T1458Z/`.
- Current profile context: fresh bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-stroke-gradient-line-profile-20260706T1458Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` as the dominant scenario at 321.155 ms p95 over 3 release-perf iterations. Stage evidence keeps `layout` first at 247.966 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 44.780 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.838 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 294.847 us p95 per stream. The golden checksum manifest passes from the bundle's `golden/` directory via `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt`.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 4, effort 2, score 6.0. SVG paint-server strokes are common in icons and generated diagrams. Full arbitrary path stroke gradients require converting stroked Beziers into fillable outlines or a PDF mask, but straight `<line>` strokes have an exact finite parallelogram/square-cap outline that can be clipped and painted with the existing native PDF shading machinery.
- Root cause: the renderer parsed `stroke="url(#gradient)"` only far enough to choose a deterministic representative fallback color. The style model had `fill_gradient` but no `stroke_gradient`, and `draw_svg_line` did not receive gradient resources or page shading state, so even the simple exact line case could not use native PDF shadings.
- Renderer change: added `stroke_gradient` to `SvgStyle`/`SvgStylePatch`, preserved it through inheritance for open line/polyline defaults, and cleared it whenever `stroke` is reassigned to `none`, a concrete color, or `currentColor`. `draw_svg_line` now receives gradient resources and, for finite non-dashed straight lines with butt or square caps, computes the stroked outline polygon, clips to that outline, registers the existing linear/radial shading resolution, and paints it with `/Shading`. Round caps, dashed lines, paths, and polylines deliberately keep the previous representative-color fallback until a full stroked-path outline implementation exists.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_gradient_paints_use_native_linear_shading_and_fallback_colors` now pins both behaviors: an arbitrary path gradient stroke still emits the deterministic representative `RG ... S` fallback, while a `stroke-linecap="butt"` straight `<line>` with `stroke="url(#line-warm)"` emits a native `/ShadingType 2` resource and a clipped stroke-outline path before `/SG... sh`.
- frankenmermaid proof: regenerated `examples/showcase-mermaid.mmd` through `/data/projects/frankenmermaid` using `cargo run -p frankenmermaid-cli --bin fm-cli -- --config examples/showcase-frankenmermaid.toml render ... --format svg --embed-source-spans`; the generated SVG in `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/stroke-gradient-line-20260706T145422Z/showcase-mermaid.svg` is byte-identical to `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` with SHA-256 `4cc1097e4435f27730e580a21d3c00140dfc0c0799881b8217cd449321aaf0b9`. Rendered `examples/showcase.md --to pdf` without any manual `--pdf-image` flag, rasterized the result with Ghostscript through `/tmp`, and visually inspected `page-03.png`; the diagram remains nonblank, centered, readable, and includes colored node outlines, routed arrows, arrowheads, the dashed edge, and the Mermaid source block.
- First-principles proof: the new native branch is a subset of existing valid output: it only fires when the stroked line can be represented as a finite filled polygon and when a supported native gradient resolves. Otherwise the existing solid representative stroke path is used. Explicit paint fallback color, CSS cascade order, fill gradients, markers, clipping, masks, transforms, opacity, selectable SVG text, WASM boundaries, and dependency-free/unsafe-free constraints are unchanged. No network, filesystem-in-core, native runtime, or third-party dependency was added.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_gradient_paints_use_native_linear_shading_and_fallback_colors --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; frankenmermaid regeneration plus byte comparison; `cargo run --bin fmd -- examples/showcase.md --to pdf --out tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/stroke-gradient-line-20260706T145422Z/showcase.pdf --json`; Ghostscript rasterization plus visual inspection of `page-03.png`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-stroke-gradient-line-profile-20260706T1458Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the profile bundle's `golden/` directory.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this expands the dependency-free SVG/PDF renderer with an exact native paint-server stroke subset while explicitly preserving fallback behavior for the unsolved arbitrary-path case. The active goal remains open because full world-class SVG still includes arbitrary stroked-path gradient outlines, richer soft filter/mask behavior, broader paint-server/image semantics, and further PDF layout/page-generation optimization.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Line Token Scratch Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T15:50:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260706T1536Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-line-token-scratch-profile-20260706T1543Z/`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-line-token-scratch-visual-20260706T1550Z/`.
- Current profile context: fresh pre-change bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-profile-20260706T1536Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 317.322 ms p95 over three release-perf iterations. Stage evidence put PDF `layout` first at 242.567 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 44.426 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.994 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 279.619 us p95 per stream.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. The current dominant stage is still layout, and source tracing showed that every physical PDF line allocated a fresh `Vec<LineTok>` plus temporary glue-adjustment vectors while mapping chosen paragraph item ranges back to styled tokens.
- Root cause: the prior paragraph scratch work reused the Knuth-Plass optimizer's buffers, but `line_tokens_for_break` still returned a newly allocated token vector per emitted line, and `glue_adjustments` built a temporary glue list plus a returned adjustment vector for each justified line. Large PDF documents emit many physical lines, so this was low-level allocation churn directly inside the hottest measured stage.
- Renderer/layout change: `LayoutCx` now owns render-call-local `line_toks` and `glue_adjustments` buffers. `line_tokens_for_break_into` clears and refills those buffers for each chosen line, and `glue_adjustments_into` computes total flexible glue with one scan and writes final per-glue adjustments into the reusable output with a second scan, preserving the previous last-glue remainder assignment without allocating the intermediate glue list.
- First-principles proof: paragraph item ranges, break choice, justification delta, glue flex math, last-glue rounding, token order, segment grouping, shaped-width calls, x-position accumulation, floating-point PDF formatting, and tagged structure emission are unchanged. Only ownership of short-lived line/adjustment buffers changed from per-line allocations to render-call-local scratch. No dependency, unsafe code, filesystem access, native runtime assumption, or WASM-incompatible behavior was added.
- Behavior proof: the post-change `pdf-large.pdf` in `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-line-token-scratch-profile-20260706T1543Z/golden/` is byte-identical to the pre-change fresh baseline with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. The post-change profile bundle's `golden_checksums.txt` validates every golden output, and `profiled_bytes_equal_normal_pdf` passed for three profiled iterations.
- Directional performance: short post-change profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-line-token-scratch-profile-20260706T1543Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 at 306.667 ms versus 317.322 ms in the immediately preceding short baseline. PDF `layout` stage p95 moved from 242.567 ms to 233.128 ms, while page-content generation also moved from 44.426 ms to 40.824 ms. Treat this as directional because both samples used only three iterations, but it supports the scored allocation-reuse lever.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md --to pdf` without manual `--pdf-image` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-line-token-scratch-visual-20260706T1550Z/showcase.pdf`, rasterized pages 3-4 with Ghostscript through `/tmp`, and inspected the resulting PNGs. The frankenmermaid diagram remains nonblank, centered, and readable with colored node outlines, routed arrows, arrowheads, and a dashed edge; the following page still shows readable blockquotes and syntax-highlighted Rust/Python/JSON/shell code.
- Verification: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-profile-20260706T1536Z`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test render_tree --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-line-token-scratch-profile-20260706T1543Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the post-change profile bundle's `golden/` directory; pre/post `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparison; `cargo test`; release-perf showcase render and Ghostscript raster visual inspection.
- Coordination note: no commit was created for this pass because `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md` already contain large pre-existing shared-checkout changes. A pathspec commit would include peer work unrelated to this narrow scratch-reuse lever.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a small profile-driven allocation cleanup in the dominant PDF layout path with byte-identical output and refreshed frankenmermaid visual proof. The active goal remains open because the full objective still includes broader world-class SVG coverage and deeper PDF layout/page-generation optimization.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Quote Extent Scan Reuse
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T16:05:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-quote-extents-profile-20260706T155935Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-quote-extents-focused-20260706T160205Z/`.
- Current profile context: the prior profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-line-token-scratch-profile-20260706T1543Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at 306.667 ms p95 over three release-perf iterations, with `layout` at 233.128 ms p95 and `page_content_stream_generation` at 40.824 ms p95. The new broad three-iteration bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-quote-extents-profile-20260706T155935Z/` reports `pdf-large` at 315.473 ms p95, `layout` at 237.567 ms p95, and `page_content_stream_generation` at 44.107 ms p95; this is within the short-run variance envelope and is not claimed as a speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. `page_content_stream_generation` remains the second major PDF writer stage, and source tracing showed a page-local duplicate pass over every placed line and every quote bar solely to produce identical blockquote extents for backgrounds and gutter bars.
- Root cause: the page content writer computed `quote_extents(placed)` once for blockquote background panels, discarded the resulting `BTreeMap`, then recomputed the same map later for gutter bar strokes. This duplicated a per-page line walk and map allocation in the measured page-content path even though both consumers intentionally use the same extents.
- Renderer change: the page loop now builds one mutable `quote_acc` map, iterates its values to paint background panels, and later passes the same accumulator to `flush_quote_bars`, which already consumes and clears it after writing decorative gutter bars.
- First-principles proof: background iteration order remains the existing `BTreeMap` value order; gutter bar ordering and coordinates are unchanged because the same map entries are reused; `flush_quote_bars` still owns the final mutable clear point; text, annotations, structure marks, clipping, SVG rendering, compression, PDF object numbering, floating-point formatting, filesystem behavior, dependencies, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: `pdf_blockquotes_have_subtle_background_and_gutter_bar` passed; `profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages` passed; the new broad profile bundle's `golden_checksums.txt` validates every golden output; both the broad profile and the focused 10-iteration `pdf-large` run produced a `pdf-large.pdf` with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-line-token-scratch-profile-20260706T1543Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf`.
- Focused performance sample: `cargo run --profile release-perf --example fmd_perf_harness -- --scenario pdf-large --iters 10 --out-dir tests/artifacts/perf/continue-quote-extents-focused-20260706T160205Z/golden` reported `pdf-large` p95 311.140 ms, with `layout` 235.010 ms p95 and `page_content_stream_generation` 43.211 ms p95. This supports "no meaningful regression" but remains too small/noisy to claim an end-to-end improvement from this one duplicate-scan cleanup.
- Verification: Agent Mail inbox check; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo test pdf_blockquotes --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-quote-extents-profile-20260706T155935Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the broad profile bundle's `golden/` directory; broad/focused `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparisons against the previous profile artifact.
- Coordination note: no commit was created for this pass because `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and many other files already contain large pre-existing shared-checkout changes. A pathspec commit would include peer work unrelated to this narrow duplicate-scan cleanup.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes redundant work from the measured PDF page-content stage with byte-identical output and no statistically meaningful regression. ## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Reference Collector Block-Aware Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T16:14:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-blockfast-focused-20260706T160912Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-blockfast-profile-20260706T161013Z/`.
- Current profile context: the previous broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-quote-extents-profile-20260706T155935Z/` ranked `parser-large` second at 27.881 ms p95, with `reference_collection` at 6.733 ms p95. The fresh broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-blockfast-profile-20260706T161013Z/` reports `parser-large` at 24.019 ms p95 and `reference_collection` at 4.319 ms p95 over three release-perf iterations; a focused 10-iteration parser sample at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-blockfast-focused-20260706T160912Z/` reports `parser-large` at 23.518 ms p95 and `reference_collection` at 4.639 ms p95.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. After the prior inline fast path, parser profiling still showed `reference_collection` as a recurring multi-millisecond stage. Source tracing showed its plain-line shortcut used the generic Markdown special-byte scanner, which treats inline-only bytes such as non-leading digits, parentheses, `!`, `&`, and `@` as blockers even though the reference collector only needs block/reference state.
- Root cause: ordinary prose lines like `Version 2.0 (draft)!` in a document that contains at least one reference candidate still fell through to `scan_markdown_line` plus block-state checks. Those inline-only bytes cannot start a reference definition, table, fence, blockquote, HTML block, list, thematic break, setext underline, or indented code line from that position, so the generic scanner was over-conservative for this collector.
- Parser change: `reference_collector_plain_line_fast_path` is now block-aware. It returns paragraph text directly for lines containing only inline-level punctuation or non-leading digits, returns non-paragraph directly for indented code, and conservatively falls back to the existing full classifier for actual block/reference candidates: tabs, pipes, leading `#`, `>`, `<`, fence markers, setext/thematic markers, unordered markers, ordered marker candidates, and leading `[...]:` definitions.
- Regression target: `reference_collector_fast_path_ignores_inline_only_punctuation` pins the new boundary: numeric/punctuated prose and inline-looking `<span>`/`[text]:` text stay on the fast path, indented code stays non-paragraph, and headings, blockquotes, fences, thematic breaks, ordered lists, table rows, reference definitions, and HTML block starts all still use the full classifier.
- First-principles proof: the fast path only changes classification cost, not block semantics. Every construct that can alter reference-definition scope or open/close paragraph state still falls back to the existing parser helpers; lines accepted by the fast path are ordinary paragraph text under the old `line_is_paragraph_text_with_scan` result. Ordering, first-definition-wins behavior, lazy-continuation rules, table-boundary preservation, nested container traversal, inline parsing, floating-point behavior, RNG, dependencies, unsafe code, filesystem behavior, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: the broad profile bundle's `golden_checksums.txt` validates every golden output; `parser-large.html` stayed byte-identical to the previous broad profile with SHA-256 `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`; `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`; the parser profile proof obligation `profiled_parse_equals_normal_parse_and_html` passed in both the focused 10-iteration and broad 3-iteration artifacts.
- Verification: Agent Mail inbox check; exclusive reservations for `src/parse/mod.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo test reference_collector_fast_path_ignores_inline_only_punctuation --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test refdef_paragraph_tests --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance profiled_parser -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance reference -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_spans -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_metamorphic -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_fuzz -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test`; focused 10-iteration `parser-large` release-perf harness; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-parser-ref-blockfast-profile-20260706T161013Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the broad profile bundle's `golden/` directory; parser/PDF golden hash comparisons against the previous broad profile artifact.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Font-Slot Text Reference Scan
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T16:32:28Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-baseline-20260706T162617Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-after-20260706T162828Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-profile-20260706T163101Z/`.
- Current profile context: the prior broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-ref-blockfast-profile-20260706T161013Z/` still ranked `pdf-large` first at 312.792 ms p95, with PDF stages dominated by `layout` at 237.965 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 43.631 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.949 ms p95, and `glyph_collection_and_shaping` at 4.105 ms p95. A fresh focused 5-iteration pre-change baseline at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-baseline-20260706T162617Z/` reported `pdf-large` at 323.584 ms p95, `glyph_collection_and_shaping` at 4.499 ms p95, and `used_slot_scan` at 0.161 ms p95.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. The target stages are not the dominant layout/page-writer costs, but they are measurable and source tracing showed repeated whole-document scans that could be removed without touching output geometry, shaping, font subsetting, PDF object ordering, or SVG rendering semantics.
- Root cause: `serialize` first discovered used font slots by scanning every line once per possible slot, then each used slot scanned every laid-out text segment and every SVG text label again to filter by that slot. This multiplies line/segment traversal by the number of font slots even though the segment order needed by glyph collection is simple and deterministic.
- Renderer change: added a render-call-local `FontSlotTextRefs` index that scans lines once, storing non-empty normal text segments and SVG text labels by existing PDF font slot. `used_slots` is now derived from that index, and glyph collection/subsetting consumes the indexed references. The collector deliberately preserves the previous per-slot order: regular laid-out segments first, then SVG text labels, matching the old two-loop sequence.
- First-principles proof: no text is reshaped in a different order within a slot, no characters or shaped glyph ids are added or removed, `BTreeSet`/`BTreeMap` ordering for subset seed glyphs and ToUnicode ligature entries is unchanged, font slot ordering is still `SLOTS`, and the emitted PDF bytes remain identical. Floating-point layout, object numbering, compression, SVG paint/text behavior, parser output, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe code, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: the focused post-change harness at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-after-20260706T162828Z/` produced a `pdf-large.pdf` with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, identical to the focused pre-change baseline. The broad post-change gauntlet at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-profile-20260706T163101Z/` also produced the same `pdf-large.pdf` hash and its `golden_checksums.txt` validated every golden output. `profiled_bytes_equal_normal_pdf` passed in both focused test and profile artifacts.
- Directional performance: the direct focused before/after samples moved `pdf-large` p95 from 323.584 ms to 315.451 ms over five iterations. The targeted support stages moved from `glyph_collection_and_shaping` 4.499 ms p95 and `used_slot_scan` 0.161 ms p95 to 4.045 ms and 0.117 ms in the focused run; the broad 3-iteration gauntlet reported 4.129 ms and 0.104 ms respectively. Treat the end-to-end delta as directional because short runs remain noisy, but the stage movement supports the scored one-lever cleanup.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Embedded-Face Slot Lookup
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T16:40:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-subset-lookup-after-20260706T163543Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-subset-lookup-profile-20260706T163835Z/`.
- Current profile context: the immediately preceding broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-profile-20260706T163101Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 315.379 ms p95, with PDF `layout` still dominant at 240.906 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` second at 42.417 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 25.246 ms p95, and `glyph_collection_and_shaping` at 4.129 ms p95. This pass targets the measured page-content writer support path, not the dominant layout algorithm.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. Every normal text segment and SVG text label in page content generation needed to find its embedded subset face by slot. The available face set is tiny, but the lookup happens for many thousands of text runs, and the replacement is a deterministic table derived from the already-built `subsets` vector.
- Root cause: `draw_seg` and `draw_svg_text` used `subsets.iter().find(|f| f.slot == slot)` on every emitted text run. After the preceding glyph-scan pass, font slot usage is already known once per render, but the page-content writer still repeated a linear search through the same immutable subset vector for each text segment and SVG label.
- Renderer change: added `EmbeddedFaceLookup`, a render-call-local `[Option<usize>; SLOTS.len()]` index populated immediately after subset construction. `draw_seg`, `draw_svg_image`, and `draw_svg_text` now receive that lookup and resolve `slot -> subset index -> &EmbeddedFace` in constant time. The subset vector, slot ordering, shaping cache, glyph mapping, kerning, string escaping, and emitted operators are unchanged.
- First-principles proof: the lookup table stores indices into the same immutable `subsets` vector that the previous linear search examined, with the same `pdf_font_slot_index` mapping used elsewhere in serialization. Missing or unexpected slots still return `None` and skip text emission as before. No text ordering, glyph shaping, subset seed order, ToUnicode ordering, PDF object numbering, floating-point math, SVG geometry, compression, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe code, or WASM portability changed.
- Behavior proof: the focused post-change release-perf harness at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-subset-lookup-after-20260706T163543Z/` produced `pdf-large.pdf` with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, identical to `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-glyphscan-profile-20260706T163101Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf`. The broad post-change gauntlet at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-subset-lookup-profile-20260706T163835Z/` produced the same `pdf-large.pdf` hash and its `golden_checksums.txt` validated every golden output. `profiled_bytes_equal_normal_pdf` passed in the focused test and profile artifacts.
- Directional performance: focused `pdf-large` p95 moved from the previous focused post-glyphscan sample's 315.451 ms to 311.207 ms over five iterations; `page_content_stream_generation` moved from 42.535 ms p95 to 42.044 ms p95. The broad 3-iteration gauntlet reported `pdf-large` 304.362 ms p95 and `page_content_stream_generation` 40.974 ms p95. Treat this as low-amplitude directional support within normal short-run variance, but it is consistent with removing repeated text-run lookup work.
- Verification: Agent Mail inbox check; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; focused post-change `pdf-large` release-perf harness; `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 comparison; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test pdf_svg_text_font_weight_and_style_select_embedded_font_slots --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-subset-lookup-profile-20260706T163835Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the broad profile bundle's `golden/` directory; broad `pdf-large.pdf` hash comparison against the previous broad profile artifact.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Empty Glue-Adjustment Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T17:01:18Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-resume-profile-20260706T1655Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-empty-adjustment-after-20260706T1700Z/`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-empty-adjustment-visual-20260706T1708Z/`.
- Fresh profile context: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-resume-profile-20260706T1655Z` ranked `pdf-large` first at 313.657 ms p95. The profile's PDF stage evidence ranked `layout` first at 227.596 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 45.040 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.926 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 278.446 us p95 per page stream. `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` passed for the profile bundle.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. `layout` remains the dominant stage, and source tracing showed every physical line called `line_tokens_for_break_into`; most non-final or non-justified lines produce no glue adjustments, but still entered the adjustment lookup path.
- Root cause: `line_tokens_for_break_into` correctly delegated adjustment computation to `glue_adjustments_into`, but then always used the adjustment-index scanner even when `adjustments` was empty. For non-justified lines, final lines, forced-break lines, and zero-delta lines, the extra branch/index work cannot affect output because every token's `extra_advance` is exactly zero.
- Renderer/layout change: added an empty-adjustment branch immediately after `glue_adjustments_into`. When no adjustments exist, line-token reconstruction copies the selected token groups with `extra_advance: 0.0`, trims trailing spaces, appends the chosen hyphen-break token if present, and returns before the adjustment scanner. The existing adjusted path is unchanged for justified lines that actually distribute stretch or shrink.
- First-principles proof: item range selection, line-break decisions, token ordering, trailing-space trimming, hyphen-break token insertion, segment grouping, shaped-width measurement, PDF text emission, SVG rendering, page serialization, compression, object ordering, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe code, and WASM portability are unchanged. The new branch is only taken when the previous adjustment lookup would have returned `0.0` for every token.
- Behavior proof: `profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages` passed, and the focused post-change release-perf harness at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-empty-adjustment-after-20260706T1700Z/golden/` produced `pdf-large.pdf` with SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, identical to the fresh baseline artifact at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-resume-profile-20260706T1655Z/golden/pdf-large.pdf`.
- Performance note: the focused five-iteration post-change sample reported `pdf-large` p95 315.987 ms and layout p95 231.711 ms, which is inside the current short-run variance envelope rather than a durable speed win. This pass is therefore recorded as a redundant-work cleanup with byte-identical proof, not as an end-to-end latency claim.
- frankenmermaid/SVG proof: current `fmd` rendered `examples/showcase.md --to pdf` without a manual `--pdf-image` flag into `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-empty-adjustment-visual-20260706T1708Z/showcase.pdf`; Ghostscript rasterized all four pages. Visual inspection of `page-03.png` showed the frankenmermaid SVG as a nonblank, centered vector diagram with readable labels, routed arrows, arrowheads, and a dashed edge into `PDF`; `page-04.png` showed readable blockquotes and visible Rust/Python/JSON/shell syntax highlighting.
