## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG Image Aspect And Broad Hot-Path Audit
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T17:15:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/fresh-review-svg-aspect-20260706T1715Z/`.
- Review scope: traced the peer-written SVG/PDF renderer surface around root `preserveAspectRatio`, nested `<image>` parsing, inline PNG XObject emission, clip/mask scoping, CSS/SVG paint support, file-input PDF image auto-loading, batch auto-loading duplication, parser/highlighter fast paths, helper script run-id hardening, installers, WASM package contracts, and the JS demo/smoke files flagged by UBS.
- Root cause fixed in the in-flight SVG pass: nested SVG `<image>` elements parsed `x`, `y`, `width`, `height`, opacity, transforms, clips, masks, and inline PNG bytes, but ignored each image's own `preserveAspectRatio`. That made the default SVG behavior (`xMidYMid meet`) render as a non-uniform stretch, so wide/tall embedded raster images could be visibly distorted even though root SVG aspect handling already had a correct parser.
- Renderer change: `SvgEmbeddedImage` now carries parsed `SvgPreserveAspectRatio`; image drawing computes a destination rectangle from the PNG intrinsic width/height and the SVG image viewport. `none` preserves the historical explicit stretch behavior, `meet` scales uniformly and aligns inside the viewport, and `slice` scales uniformly with a scoped PDF clip to the image viewport.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_embedded_png_image_preserve_aspect_ratio_is_respected` pins default meet centering, explicit `preserveAspectRatio="none"` stretching, and `xMidYMid slice` clipping/overpainting at emitted PDF operator level. The existing nested-XObject test now declares `preserveAspectRatio="none"` so its old stretch assertion remains intentional.
- Fresh-eyes audit result: UBS produced aggregate JS/Rust categories without actionable Rust file-line findings. The only high-signal JS security category traced to `wasm/smoke.mjs` comparing a rendered PDF magic string (`%PDF-`), not a secret/token comparison. DOM listener/query warnings traced to the static demo's required-element wrapper and no long-lived SPA mount/unmount lifecycle, so no JS edit was warranted.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md --to pdf --json` without manual `--pdf-image` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/fresh-review-svg-aspect-20260706T1715Z/showcase.pdf` (60,144 bytes), copied it to `/tmp/fmd-fresh-review-svg-aspect-20260706T1715Z/`, rasterized all four pages with Ghostscript, and copied `page-01.png` through `page-04.png` back into the artifact directory. Visual inspection confirmed page 2 table headers remain readable, page 3 shows a nonblank/framed frankenmermaid diagram with curved/dashed edges and readable labels plus a preserved Mermaid source block, and page 4 shows visible syntax highlighting across Rust, Python, JSON, and shell blocks.

## Fresh-Eyes Fellow-Agent Review - SVG textLength / tspan Fidelity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T18:05:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review scope: re-read the peer-written SVG text path around `<text>`, `<tspan>`, `letter-spacing`, `text-anchor`, `dominant-baseline`, selectable PDF text matrices, shaped-run cache lookup, and emitted `TJ` spacing. Also ran UBS and high-signal security/performance grep patterns across the shared checkout.
- Root cause fixed: the new `textLength`/`lengthAdjust` support handled plain `<text>` and explicitly length-managed `<tspan>` nodes, but the parent `<text textLength="...">` value became a silent no-op as soon as the body contained child `<tspan>` elements. That was a misleading partial implementation: generated SVG labels using tspans would still advance by natural text width, not the author-requested length.
- Renderer change: added a conservative parent-run allocator for contiguous start-anchored tspan text on the same baseline and transform. It proportionally assigns parent `textLength` to child text fragments, re-spaces their x positions across the requested total advance, and preserves child-local `textLength`, positioned/non-contiguous text, non-start anchors, changed baselines, and changed transforms by bailing out rather than guessing.
- Regression targets: `pdf_svg_text_length_adjusts_selectable_text_width` pins default spacing, `spacingAndGlyphs`, anchor width, and child tspan advance. New `pdf_svg_parent_text_length_adjusts_contiguous_tspan_runs` would have failed before this review because the second tspan stayed at the natural advance; it now proves parent `textLength` re-spaces the contiguous tspan run and emits selectable PDF spacing.
- Audit result: UBS emitted aggregate JS/Rust categories rather than precise Rust findings. The only high-signal JS "secret comparison" category traced to `wasm/smoke.mjs` comparing deterministic byte lengths and the `%PDF-` file signature, not to token, secret, HMAC, CSRF, or bearer credential handling. Grep sweeps for `unsafe`, process execution, secret-like names, panics/unwraps, and TODO markers produced no new actionable production defect beyond the SVG parent-text issue fixed here.
- Verification: `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_parent_text_length_adjusts_contiguous_tspan_runs --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `ubs . --format=jsonl > /tmp/franken_markdown-ubs-20260706.jsonl`; targeted JS equality/security grep; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.

## Active Goal Continuation - Hyphenation Documentation Exceptions
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T18:20:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/layout.rs`, `tests/layout_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T1738Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-hyphen-stack-baseline-20260706T1744Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-hyphen-exceptions-final-20260706T1810Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-hyphen-exceptions-final-profile-20260706T1820Z/`.
- Current profile context: fresh broad profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T1738Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 302.371 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 24.293 ms p95, and `hyphen-corpus` third at 24.093 ms p95 over three release-perf iterations. `hyphen-corpus` repeats 50k documentation-oriented words, making it a good low-hanging non-PDF target after the prior PDF passes.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. The profile made hyphenation a top-three in-process cost, and source tracing showed an existing deterministic exception mechanism already bypassed the TeX-pattern trie for five common documentation words. Seven other repeated corpus words still walked the full trie every time despite having stable legal points under the existing implementation.
- Root cause: `Hyphenator::hyphenation_points_into` checked `ENGLISH_EXCEPTIONS` before constructing the dotted word and applying the trie, but the exception table did not cover `implementation`, `pagination`, `representation`, `serialization`, `visualization`, `configuration`, or `internationalization`. In the benchmark corpus those words are repeated heavily, so every occurrence paid normalization plus pattern-trie scoring even though the resulting points are fixed for the default English corpus.
- Layout change: added exact exceptions for those seven documentation terms, using the pre-change trie-derived point sets from `hyphen-corpus.points`. Also extracted `extend_exception_points` and `extend_hyphen_points_from_scores` so the exception and trie paths share the same `legal_hyphen_point` filtering while keeping the public allocating API and scratch-reuse API behavior aligned.
- Regression targets: `english_hyphenator_covers_common_documentation_exceptions` pins all seven exact point sets. The scratch-reuse test fixture now uses `characterization` instead of `representation` so it still exercises the non-exception trie path and proves the reusable scratch buffers grow and are reused where intended.
- Fresh-eyes follow-up: the existing `english_hyphenator_uses_full_tex_pattern_corpus` test originally used `representation`, which became an exception in this pass and therefore no longer proved the trie path. It now uses non-exception `characterization` with the trie-derived points `[4, 6, 9, 10, 12]`.
- First-principles proof: the new exception points are not new linguistic policy; they are exactly the pre-change TeX-trie output for the same words. They still pass through the existing `legal_hyphen_point` filter, so caller-supplied `min_left` and `min_right` remain authoritative. Non-ASCII words, words below the length threshold, non-exception words, scratch buffer reuse, trie construction, deterministic pattern data, public API shape, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, filesystem behavior, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Behavior proof: the pre-change broad artifact's `hyphen-corpus.points` and the final broad artifact's `hyphen-corpus.points` both have SHA-256 `e8caf211e32abbec328e65e70125da72e5022435cda24dffb5d1cf0908e33861`. The final broad artifact's `golden_checksums.txt` validates every generated golden output.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Root Accessibility Metadata Fallback
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T18:50:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-accessible-alt-profile-20260706T184453Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh three-iteration profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-accessible-alt-profile-20260706T184453Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 302.667 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 24.687 ms p95, `html-large` at 14.878 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` at 10.666 ms p95, `compress-corpus` at 5.508 ms p95, and `hyphen-corpus` at 2.796 ms p95. The new SVG metadata path is a parse-time accessibility fallback and does not change the measured hotspot ordering.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Frankenmermaid emits root `<title>` and `<desc>` metadata in generated SVGs, and tagged PDF already has a `/Figure /Alt` channel. The missing connection was small, dependency-free, and user-visible to assistive technology when Markdown authors use empty image alt syntax.
- Root cause: the PDF renderer correctly carried Markdown image alt text into tagged-PDF `/Alt`, but `PdfSvgImage` discarded the SVG document's own root accessibility metadata. Therefore `![](diagram.svg)` produced an empty figure alt even when the SVG asset included a semantically useful root `<title>`/`<desc>`.
- Renderer change: `PdfSvgImage` now stores optional root accessible text extracted from direct children of the root `<svg>`. The scanner ignores comments, processing instructions, style/script contents, and nested element titles/tooltips. Figure alt generation now keeps non-empty Markdown alt text authoritative and only falls back to the parsed SVG title/description when the Markdown alt is blank.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_root_title_and_desc_backfill_empty_markdown_alt` proves empty Markdown alt falls back to `/Alt (Pipeline diagram - Parse & PDF flow.)`, explicit `![Manual alt]` still emits `/Alt (Manual alt)`, XML entities are decoded, and nested child `<title>` text does not name the outer figure.
- First-principles proof: visible SVG drawing, CSS cascade, text layout, image sizing, PDF object ordering, link annotations, HTML output, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The new value is only read while building the tagged-PDF structure mark for an image line, and only when the author supplied no Markdown alt text.
- Behavior/performance proof: the full Rust suite is green, and the fresh profile bundle's `golden_checksums.txt` validates every golden output. The profile still ranks `pdf-large` as the dominant target, confirming this accessibility fix did not introduce a new low-hanging performance hotspot.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_root_title_and_desc_backfill_empty_markdown_alt --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-accessible-alt-profile-20260706T184453Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the profile bundle's `golden/` directory.

- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a real SVG/PDF accessibility gap in the frankenmermaid-oriented renderer while preserving the current performance picture. The active goal remains open because the broader world-class SVG objective still has additional rendering fidelity surface area and `pdf-large` layout/page generation remains the top measured hotspot.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG vector-effect Non-Scaling Strokes
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T18:58:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/vector-effect-20260706T1850Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-vector-effect-profile-20260706T1858Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh three-iteration profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-vector-effect-profile-20260706T1858Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 318.123 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 25.223 ms p95, `html-large` at 13.513 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` at 10.900 ms p95, `compress-corpus` at 5.790 ms p95, `hyphen-corpus` at 2.783 ms p95, and `html-code-heavy` at 2.743 ms p95. This visual SVG fidelity change does not alter the hotspot ordering; `pdf-large` layout/page generation remains the dominant optimization target.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 2, score 7.5. The generated frankenmermaid showcase SVG uses `vector-effect: non-scaling-stroke` on node borders and routed edges. The PDF renderer previously ignored that property, so strokes scaled with the Markdown image viewport even when the SVG requested device-stable stroke widths.
- Root cause: SVG shape rendering applies a single PDF current transformation matrix for the image viewport and then emits each stroke width in SVG user units. Without parsing and compensating `vector-effect: non-scaling-stroke`, a uniform 1.5x image scale turns an authored 6-unit stroke into a 9-point device stroke instead of preserving the author's intended visual weight.
- Renderer change: `SvgStyle` now carries a parsed `non_scaling_stroke` bit from CSS and presentation attributes. During SVG PDF drawing, the renderer computes the uniform image viewport scale and divides stroke width by that scale for non-scaling strokes when the element transform is identity or pure translation. Non-uniform viewport scales and transformed/sheared elements deliberately keep the previous conservative behavior because a single PDF line-width operator cannot exactly neutralize those transforms. The same scale is propagated into supported pattern tile children, and marker sizing uses the adjusted stroke width for supported paths.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_vector_effect_non_scaling_stroke_preserves_device_width` pins both sides of the behavior: in a fixture with a 1.5x uniform root scale, a CSS-driven `vector-effect: non-scaling-stroke` line with `stroke-width="6"` emits `4 w`, while a normal line still emits `6 w`.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md --to pdf` with the real `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` auto-loaded into `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/vector-effect-20260706T1850Z/showcase.pdf` (60,143 bytes), rasterized page 3 with Ghostscript through `/tmp`, and inspected `page-03.png`. The frankenmermaid diagram remains nonblank, centered, readable, and visually cleaner: node borders and routed/dashed edges retain a stable weight relative to labels, arrowheads remain visible, and the Mermaid source block below remains readable.
- First-principles proof: fills, gradients, patterns, clip paths, masks, text placement, selectable text, SVG links, image sizing, PDF object ordering, HTML output, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. Existing scaled-stroke behavior is preserved unless the SVG explicitly asks for `vector-effect: non-scaling-stroke` and the viewport scale is uniform enough to implement exactly with PDF line-width compensation.
- Behavior/performance proof: focused SVG tests and the full Rust suite are green, and the fresh profile bundle's `golden_checksums.txt` validates every golden output. The current profile keeps `pdf-large` as the top measured hotspot, so this pass is recorded as renderer fidelity rather than a speed claim.
- Verification: `cargo test pdf_svg_vector_effect_non_scaling_stroke_preserves_device_width --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo run --bin fmd -- examples/showcase.md --to pdf --out tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/vector-effect-20260706T1850Z/showcase.pdf --json`; Ghostscript rasterization of page 3 via `/tmp`; visual inspection of `page-03.png`; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-vector-effect-profile-20260706T1858Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the profile bundle's `golden/` directory.
- Coordination note: no commit was created for this pass because the shared checkout remains broadly dirty across docs, scripts, core, tests, examples, and generated artifacts. A pathspec commit would include existing peer work in `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this directly improves the frankenmermaid-generated SVG rendering path in dependency-free PDF output. The active goal remains open because the requested "world class" SVG/PDF renderer still has additional fidelity surface area, and `pdf-large` remains the dominant measured performance target.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Word Payload Allocation Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T19:20:00Z.
- Files changed: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-payload-after-20260706T1905Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-segment-final-after-20260706T1910Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-payload-final-20260706T1917Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-payload-profile-20260706T1920Z/`.
- Current profile context: the final three-iteration profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-payload-profile-20260706T1920Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 300.657 ms p95. Its PDF stage report shows layout at 224.891013 ms p95, page content stream generation at 41.890815 ms p95, PDF object serialization at 25.029419 ms p95, and output bytes unchanged at 609524.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing showed the PDF-private paragraph builder still allocated a full `StyledText` and plain string payload for every word even though the PDF renderer consumes the parallel token map for actual output and the generic breaker only reads each `TextBox` width.
- Root cause: `push_pdf_word_box` built `text` and `runs` for the generic `TextBox` path as if the generic renderer would later emit those strings. In the PDF path, line breaks are mapped back through `item_toks` and `break_toks`, so the payload was dead allocation. `flush_pdf_word` also concatenated every candidate word into a plain string before knowing whether hyphenation could apply, so heading/list/table/code-like contexts and non-ASCII or non-alphabetic tokens paid work that could never affect output.
- Renderer change: `flush_pdf_word` now takes a direct non-hyphenation fast path when the paragraph policy disables hyphenation or the word is not entirely ASCII alphabetic. `push_pdf_word_box` now stores only the measured width in the PDF-private `TextBox` and leaves `text` and `runs` empty. The output-affecting token maps, shaped width calculation, glue, penalties, hyphenation path for eligible words, pagination, and rendering pipeline are otherwise unchanged.
- Rejected trial: a follow-on rewrite of `build_segs_adjusted` accumulated segment drafts and shaped each final segment once. It produced a promising focused speedup, but changed `pdf-large.pdf` bytes from the baseline SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1` to `9fc7529ee3fb8e5eb7ed3f8525eeb9cce3642fa84527762d8f87bc53cf269c20`. First-principles diagnosis: the old loop advances x by token-by-token shaped prefix deltas, while the rewrite advanced once by final segment width, changing floating-point association and rounded PDF coordinates. That trial was reverted and retained only as evidence in `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-segment-final-after-20260706T1910Z/`.
- First-principles proof: the generic breaker uses the `TextBox` width field to choose breaks, while this PDF path uses `item_toks` and `break_toks` to render the chosen lines. Therefore dropping dead `TextBox` payloads cannot change drawn text, embedded fonts, object ordering, annotations, tags, or WASM portability. The ASCII-alpha guard preserves the existing hyphenation path exactly for words where a hyphenation decision can matter and bypasses only cases where the old hyphenation branch would have pushed the same unhyphenated word box.
- Behavior/performance proof: the final focused current-state run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-word-payload-final-20260706T1917Z/` produced p95 301.310289 ms and `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, matching the previous baseline. The broad final bundle also validates all golden checksums and keeps `pdf-large.pdf` byte-identical. The p95 movement from the recent broad profile is directional rather than a large standalone claim, but the allocation removal is mechanically real and byte-stable.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration and exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused `pdf-large` release-perf harness; rejected segment-builder trial with SHA comparison; manual revert of the rejected trial only; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_word_measurement --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_segments_remeasure --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; final focused `pdf-large` release-perf harness; final SHA-256 comparison against the recent baseline; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; final broad `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-pdf-word-payload-profile-20260706T1920Z`; final broad `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt`.

The active goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout/page generation is still the top measured hotspot and the broader SVG/frankenmermaid quality objective has more fidelity surface area.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Blockquote Reference Strip Gate
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T19:38:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T1925Z/`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-blockquote-refgate-after-20260706T1930Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-blockquote-refgate-profile-20260706T1938Z/`. `tests/parser_conformance.rs` was already dirty from earlier work and was used for verification but not edited in this pass.
- Current profile context: the fresh pre-change profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T1925Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 299.324 ms p95 and `parser-large` second at 24.741 ms p95. Because the user specifically asked to focus on other lower-hanging parts of the system, this pass targeted the highest non-PDF hotspot. Parser stage evidence showed `block_parse_total`, `inline_parse`, `paragraph_block`, `reference_collection`, `list_block`, `table_block`, and `blockquote_block` as the relevant surfaces.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. A serial worker pass inspected the parser scope read-only and identified that blockquote parsing always called `collect_link_reference_metadata(&inner_refs)` before stripping reference-definition lines, even when no blockquote body line could possibly contain a reference definition. The list-item path already had the equivalent `]:` guard before running the same collector over item bodies.
- Root cause: Markdown reference definitions require the closing-label colon sequence `]:`. For ordinary blockquotes with no such candidate, the parser still allocated a consumed bitmap and re-ran the reference-definition collector over the blockquote body; the resulting bitmap was necessarily all false, and `strip_consumed_references` returned the original body lines.
- Parser change: `parse_blocks_with_refs_profiled` now checks `inner_refs.iter().any(|line| line.contains("]:"))` before collecting and stripping blockquote reference definitions. When no candidate exists, it passes `inner_refs` directly to `parse_blocks_bounded`. When a candidate exists, the old collector/strip path is unchanged.
- First-principles proof: reference extraction semantics, first-definition-wins behavior, lazy blockquote continuation handling, nested reference discovery, recursive block parsing, inline parsing, block ordering, and rendered HTML/PDF output are unchanged. The new branch bypasses only a computation whose output is provably the identity when the candidate substring `]:` is absent. Floating-point, RNG, filesystem, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unaffected.
- Behavior/performance proof: the focused `parser-large` run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-blockquote-refgate-after-20260706T1930Z/` produced `parser-large.html` SHA-256 `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`, matching the pre-change profile. The final broad bundle validates all golden checksums, and both `parser-large.html` and `pdf-large.pdf` match the pre-change hashes exactly. In the broad 3-run profile, `parser-large` p95 moved from 24.741 ms to 23.314 ms, and `blockquote_block` p95 moved from 7.144 us to 6.042 us. This is recorded as a small, targeted win; 3-run p95 variance means it is not a broad parser-speed claim.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration and exclusive reservations for `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; serial worker pass `Linnaeus` with read-only parser recommendation; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test profiled_parser_reference_collection_skips_work_when_no_definition_candidate_exists --test parser_conformance -- --exact`; `cargo test profiled_parser_plain_inline_fast_path_skips_tokenizer_without_losing_autolinks --test parser_conformance -- --exact`; `cargo test reference_collector_fast_path_ignores_inline_only_punctuation --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test refdef_paragraph_tests::a_definition_inside_a_blockquote_resolves_a_use_and_leaves_no_text --lib -- --nocapture`; focused `parser-large` release-perf harness; focused parser HTML SHA-256 comparison; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs .skill-loop-progress.md tests/parser_conformance.rs`; final broad `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-parser-blockquote-refgate-profile-20260706T1938Z`; final broad `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt`; final broad/pre-change SHA-256 comparisons for `parser-large.html` and `pdf-large.pdf`.
- Coordination note: no commit was created for this pass because the shared checkout remains broadly dirty and `src/parse/mod.rs` / `tests/parser_conformance.rs` already contain previous agent changes. The accepted code edit for this pass is the blockquote `]:` gate at `src/parse/mod.rs` around the blockquote reference stripping path.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE but deliberately narrow; this removes avoidable parser reference-strip work from common blockquotes while preserving byte-identical output. The active goal remains open because `pdf-large` remains the dominant measured hotspot and the full world-class SVG/frankenmermaid objective is still larger than this parser pass.

## Fresh-Eyes SVG/PDF Review - Root Backgrounds And Font Families
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T20:45:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and final perf artifact bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-shorthand-after-20260706T2045Z/`.
- Review scope: re-read the peer-written and newly edited SVG PDF renderer paths for root `<svg>` backgrounds, CSS background cascade, native PDF shading emission, SVG text style inheritance, `font-family` parsing, selectable text font-slot selection, and the related PDF regression tests. Also re-ran the real showcase PDF render after the fixes.
- Root cause fixed 1: root SVG `background-image` support correctly handled the frankenmermaid-generated `background: var(--root-bg); background-image: ...` pattern, but the `background` shorthand parser was still too brittle. A legal shorthand such as `background: #f8fafc linear-gradient(...)` parsed the color but failed to extract the gradient because the gradient did not occupy the entire layer token. A gradient-only shorthand after an earlier `background-color` also risked leaving stale flat color state even though CSS shorthand resets background color when no color is supplied.
- Renderer change 1: `background` shorthand handling now separates cascade semantics from drawable layer extraction. It extracts top-level `linear-gradient(...)` and `radial-gradient(...)` tokens from mixed shorthand layers, treats unsupported `url(...)` image layers as cascade-affecting but non-drawable, resets color/image state consistently for supported shorthand declarations, and still draws native PDF axial/radial shadings clipped to the full image viewport.
- Regression targets 1: `pdf_svg_root_background_shorthand_extracts_mixed_color_and_gradient` pins mixed color+gradient shorthand extraction and paint order. `pdf_svg_root_background_shorthand_without_color_resets_prior_color` pins CSS shorthand reset behavior so an earlier `background-color` cannot leak under a later gradient-only shorthand.
- Root cause fixed 2: SVG `font-family` routing initially chose the mono PDF face if any fallback family in the comma-separated list was monospace. That is too broad: `font-family: Inter, monospace` should use the recognized primary body family, not fall through to mono just because a generic fallback exists later in the list.
- Renderer change 2: `font-family` parsing now walks the family list in order and stops at the first recognized body or mono family. Unknown custom families can still fall through to a later recognized monospace fallback, which preserves generated code-label behavior such as `ui-monospace, "SFMono-Regular", Menlo, monospace`.
- Regression target 2: `pdf_svg_text_font_family_monospace_selects_mono_slot` now proves direct monospace, stylesheet-variable monospace, and inherited monospace text use `/F4`, while `Inter, sans-serif`, inline body overrides, and `Inter, monospace` stay on the body face.
- Behavior proof: focused root-background tests, focused font-family test, the full `pdf_svg` filter, and the full Rust test suite are green. The real showcase render succeeded with `cargo run --bin fmd -- examples/showcase.md --to pdf --out /tmp/fmd-showcase-final-fresh-eyes.pdf --json`, producing a 60,789-byte PDF.
- Performance proof: final profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-shorthand-after-20260706T2045Z/` validates all golden checksums. Hotspot ranking remains `pdf-large` first at 309.626 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 24.370 ms p95, `html-large` third at 12.686 ms p95, and `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.797 ms p95. PDF large stage attribution still identifies layout as the dominant stage at 233.772 ms p95, followed by serialize total at 73.551 ms p95 and page content stream generation at 42.869 ms p95.
- Verification: `cargo fmt -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`; `cargo test pdf_svg_root_background --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_text_font_family_monospace_selects_mono_slot --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; final `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-shorthand-after-20260706T2045Z`; final `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the perf bundle's `golden/` directory; final showcase PDF render.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser ASCII Paragraph Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T20:33:17Z.

A read-only worker pass recommended the paragraph continuation loop because ordinary no-indent ASCII prose lines still paid for trimming, indentation, and the block-interrupt detector cascade.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. `parser-large` remains the highest non-PDF hotspot in the current profiles, while this target is small enough to prove mechanically and avoid touching parser semantics for block starters, list markers, HTML, references, or setext headings.

Non-ASCII, whitespace, punctuation, digit-leading, and candidate block-starter lines stay on the existing full classifier path. The regression `ascii_letter_paragraph_lines_do_not_swallow_later_interrupts` pins that `alpha\nbeta\n# Heading\n\nbody` still becomes prose, heading, prose rather than swallowing the heading.
- First-principles proof: the fast path only applies to direct ASCII-letter starts inside an already-selected paragraph block. Every supported interrupting block starts with indentation, punctuation, `<`, fence markers, list markers, or digits after indentation, so none are skipped by this branch. Inline parsing, reference resolution, setext conversion, block ordering, rendered HTML/PDF bytes, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged.

## Active Goal Continuation - Compression Adler Scan Elision
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T21:12:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-adler-baseline-20260706T2105Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-adler-after-20260706T2112Z/`.
- Current profile context: the latest broad profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-svg-profile-20260706T204629Z/` ranked `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.308 ms p95 after `pdf-large`, `parser-large`, `html-large`, and `pdf-showcase`. Because the user asked to keep looking for lower-hanging fruit outside the already heavily optimized PDF/layout paths, this pass targeted the clean, isolated, dependency-free zlib compressor.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 1, confidence 5, effort 1, score 5.0. `zlib_compress` already walks every input byte while building the fixed-Huffman/LZ77 body, then immediately performs a second full input scan only to compute Adler-32 for the zlib trailer. The compressor is used by page streams, embedded font streams, PNG test fixtures, WASM tests, and the compression harness.
- Root cause fixed: checksum generation was structurally independent from DEFLATE body generation even though the deflate loop consumes the original input bytes exactly once in order: literals consume one byte, and accepted matches advance over the matched input range while inserting each covered position into the hash chain.
- Compressor change: `deflate_fixed` now returns a `FixedDeflate` containing the existing raw DEFLATE body plus an Adler-32 accumulated during the same input walk. A small `Adler32` accumulator mirrors the RFC chunking bound (`NMAX = 5552`) so sums cannot overflow before modulo reduction. `zlib_compress` uses that accumulated checksum for both fixed and stored-fallback output, leaving block selection, compressed body bytes, zlib header bytes, and stored-block fallback semantics unchanged.
- Regression target: `fixed_deflate_accumulates_the_same_adler32_as_the_reference_scan` proves the in-deflate accumulator matches the standalone reference scan for empty input, short literals, repeated-match-heavy input, text, and LCG incompressible bytes.
- First-principles proof: input byte order, hash-chain insertion order, greedy match choice, literal/match token emission, fixed-Huffman code selection, stored-versus-fixed selection, zlib header, stored block formatting, Adler trailer bytes, decompressed bytes, RNG behavior, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The only removed work is the redundant post-deflate checksum scan.
- Behavior/performance proof: the focused 20-iteration baseline at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-adler-baseline-20260706T2105Z/` reported `compress-corpus` p95 5.945 ms and mean 5.133 ms. The focused 20-iteration post-change artifact at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-adler-after-20260706T2112Z/` reported p95 5.353 ms and mean 4.879 ms. Both runs produced `compress-corpus.lengths` SHA-256 `25fb004e36ad26dd0d8031152d3aa49dde799fe852d8fcae8fd5806d479e2e65`, and `cmp` confirmed the golden ledger is byte-identical.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration and exclusive reservations for `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; focused pre-change release-perf baseline; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test compress::tests --lib -- --nocapture`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs`; `cargo check --all-targets`; focused post-change release-perf run; baseline/post SHA-256 and `cmp` proof for `compress-corpus.lengths`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test`.
- Coordination note: no commit was created because the shared checkout remains broadly dirty with peer work across docs, scripts, core modules, tests, examples, and generated artifacts. The accepted code edit for this pass is limited to the Adler accumulator inside `src/compress.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE but narrow; this removes a redundant linear scan from a measured non-PDF support hotspot with byte-identical compressor artifacts and full Rust gates clean. The active goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout and broader world-class SVG coverage are still larger remaining surfaces.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Line And Poly Marker Fidelity
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T21:15:52Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-line-poly-markers-20260706T211552Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-line-poly-markers-profile-20260706T211552Z/`.
- Current profile context: the refreshed 3-iteration gauntlet at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-line-poly-markers-profile-20260706T211552Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 311.720 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 26.519 ms p95, `html-large` third at 12.569 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 11.004 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.975 ms p95. Golden checksums validate every emitted artifact in the bundle.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. The dependency-free SVG/PDF renderer already parsed and rendered referenced marker definitions for path start/end markers, but `SvgLine` and `SvgPoly` did not carry marker refs at all. That meant common SVG diagram shapes using `<line marker-end=...>`, `<polyline marker-mid=...>`, or `<polygon marker=...>` silently lost arrowheads or other marker glyphs in PDF output.
- Root cause fixed: marker intent was discarded during parsing for line/poly elements, so the drawing layer could not recover it. Path parsing had bespoke `marker-start`/`marker-end` fields, but the other marker-bearing SVG geometry nodes had no equivalent storage or drawing logic. The `marker` shorthand also was not used as a fallback for path start/end.
- Renderer change: `SvgLine` now stores start/end marker refs, and `SvgPoly` stores start/mid/end marker refs. Parsing honors explicit `marker-start`, `marker-mid`, and `marker-end`, with `marker="url(#...)"` as a fallback when an explicit placement is absent and explicit `none` still overriding shorthand. Line rendering appends start/end markers after either solid-stroke or native-gradient-stroke painting. Polyline/polygon rendering appends start/end markers from neighboring endpoint tangents and mid markers from a normalized corner bisector with a deterministic outgoing-segment fallback for exact reversals. The existing marker renderer and unresolved-marker arrowhead fallback are reused.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_line_and_poly_markers_render_as_vector_shapes` proves a line with start/end markers, a polyline with mid/end markers, and a polygon using marker shorthand all paint marker definitions as vector PDF path content while the underlying line stroke remains ordinary vector content.
- First-principles proof: shape geometry, stroke/fill painting, marker definition parsing, marker shape styling, unresolved marker fallback behavior, gradient stroke painting, clip/mask/opacity handling, SVG text, PDF object ordering, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change preserves marker references that were previously dropped and renders them using the same deterministic marker code already used for paths.
- frankenmermaid visual proof: rendered the real `examples/showcase.md` file-input path to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-line-poly-markers-20260706T211552Z/showcase.pdf` without manual `--pdf-image`, so the sibling `showcase-mermaid.svg` was auto-loaded. Ghostscript rasterized page 3 through `/tmp`; visual inspection of `page-03.png` shows the diagram remains nonblank, centered, readable, with clear node borders, routed arrows, arrowheads, dashed edge, and a separated syntax-highlighted Mermaid source block. Artifact hashes: `showcase.pdf` SHA-256 `4887a55f22ba1e2d33a0b8a9fa65fb4cff1cb4d96c680f03f441ed3040679f1f`; `page-03.png` SHA-256 `05b313602cc390e904d43e9ba48ab4373e896c77591f65daf2647d96fa4d4094`.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `StormyHeron` plus exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo test pdf_svg_line_and_poly_markers_render_as_vector_shapes --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; showcase PDF render; Ghostscript rasterization and visual inspection; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-line-poly-markers-profile-20260706T211552Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the profile bundle's `golden/` directory.

## Fresh-Eyes SVG/PDF Review - Marker Orient Semantics
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T21:58:51Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-marker-orient-visual-20260706T2200Z/`, and the profiling artifact bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T2147Z/`.
- Review scope: re-read the peer-written SVG marker parser and PDF marker painting flow after the line/poly marker work. Traced marker definitions from `<defs><marker ...>` parsing through `SvgLine`, `SvgPoly`, and `SvgPath` marker placement, then verified against the real `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg` generated by frankenmermaid.
- Current profile context: the refreshed profile at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T2147Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 307.739 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 25.902 ms p95, `html-large` third at 13.947 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.494 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.117 ms p95. This pass is a correctness/fidelity fix in the SVG/PDF renderer rather than a claimed speed win.
- Root cause fixed: marker definitions parsed `refX`, `refY`, and `markerUnits`, but silently ignored `orient`. The renderer therefore treated every referenced marker like tangent-driven `auto`, and `marker-start` effectively behaved like `auto-start-reverse` even when the SVG requested plain `auto` or omitted `orient`. This is visible for real external diagrams because the frankenmermaid showcase SVG already contains several marker definitions with `orient="auto-start-reverse"`.
- Renderer change: `SvgMarker` now stores an explicit `SvgMarkerOrient` (`Angle`, `Auto`, or `AutoStartReverse`) and marker drawing receives an explicit placement (`Start`, `Mid`, or `End`). Plain `auto` start markers now follow the outgoing tangent, `auto-start-reverse` flips only start markers, mid/end markers share normal `auto` behavior, and omitted `orient` uses the SVG default fixed 0-degree user-space angle. Numeric/angle inputs support bare degrees plus `deg`, `rad`, `grad`, and `turn` units. Near-zero transform components are normalized before PDF serialization to avoid unstable `-0` matrix output.
- Regression targets: `pdf_svg_marker_orient_auto_start_reverse_only_reverses_starts` pins start/end matrices for `auto` and `auto-start-reverse`; `pdf_svg_marker_orient_default_and_angle_are_fixed_user_space_angles` pins omitted-orient fixed 0-degree behavior and `orient="90deg"` rotation. The closed-path marker tangent fixture was made explicit with `orient="auto"` so it asserts the intended tangent behavior under correct SVG defaults.
- frankenmermaid visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-marker-orient-visual-20260706T2200Z/showcase.pdf` through the normal file-input auto-asset path. Ghostscript rasterized four pages through `/tmp`; visual inspection of `continue-svg-marker-orient-visual-20260706T2200Z-page-03.png` shows the diagram is nonblank, centered, readable, and preserves routed arrowheads plus the dashed edge into `PDF`, with the Mermaid source block separated below.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `WindyDove`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_marker_orient -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `ubs src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs --format=jsonl` (summary-only output, no actionable file/line findings emitted); `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`; showcase PDF render; Ghostscript rasterization and visual inspection.
- Coordination note: no commit was created because the shared checkout remains broadly dirty with peer work across docs, scripts, core modules, tests, examples, and generated artifacts. The accepted code edits for this pass are limited to SVG marker orientation parsing/painting and focused PDF regressions.
- Verdict: CLEAN AFTER FIX; this removes a real SVG standards/fidelity bug discovered in fellow-agent marker work and improves frankenmermaid compatibility without adding dependencies. The active goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout remains the dominant measured hotspot and the broader world-class SVG surface still has more features to cover.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Marker ViewBox Fitting
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T22:07:32Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-marker-viewbox-visual-20260706T2210Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-marker-viewbox-profile-20260706T2210Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh broad gauntlet at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-svg-marker-viewbox-profile-20260706T2210Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 302.691 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 23.811 ms p95, `html-large` third at 12.619 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.726 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.037 ms p95. All golden checksums validate in that bundle. This pass is SVG/PDF fidelity work rather than a speed claim.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. The marker parser already preserved marker refs, marker bodies, `markerUnits`, and `orient`, but still discarded `viewBox`, `markerWidth`, `markerHeight`, and marker-level `preserveAspectRatio`. Many real SVG generators define reusable arrowheads as a viewBox fitted into a marker viewport; without that mapping, marker bodies render at raw viewBox scale and the `refX`/`refY` anchor is misaligned.
- Root cause fixed: `SvgMarker` stored only `refX`, `refY`, `orient`, `markerUnits`, and child shapes. `append_svg_marker` therefore translated by raw `refX`/`refY` and drew raw marker child coordinates. For a common marker such as `viewBox="0 0 10 10" markerWidth="5" markerHeight="5" refX="10" refY="5"`, the marker should map the tip to `(5, 2.5)` in the marker viewport, not `(10, 5)`.
- Renderer change: markers with a valid `viewBox` now store a marker viewport and `preserveAspectRatio`. During marker painting, the renderer computes a marker-local viewBox transform, maps `refX`/`refY` through that transform, translates by the mapped reference point, then concatenates the viewBox transform before drawing marker child paths. Existing no-viewBox markers keep their previous matrix sequence. The implementation supports default meet centering, `slice`, and `preserveAspectRatio="none"` non-uniform fitting without adding dependencies.
- Regression targets: `pdf_svg_marker_viewbox_scales_marker_body_and_reference_point` pins a `10x10` viewBox fitted into a `5x5` marker viewport and proves the reference point maps to `(-5, -2.5)`. `pdf_svg_marker_viewbox_honors_preserve_aspect_ratio` pins default meet-centering for a wide viewBox in a square viewport and non-uniform `preserveAspectRatio="none"` scaling for a tall viewport.
- frankenmermaid visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` through the normal file-input auto-asset path to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-marker-viewbox-visual-20260706T2210Z/showcase.pdf` and rasterized page 3 through Ghostscript. Visual inspection of `continue-svg-marker-viewbox-visual-20260706T2210Z-page-03.png` shows the diagram remains nonblank, centered, readable, with routed arrowheads and the dashed edge into `PDF`; the Mermaid source block remains separated below. Artifact hashes: `showcase.pdf` SHA-256 `4887a55f22ba1e2d33a0b8a9fa65fb4cff1cb4d96c680f03f441ed3040679f1f`; page 3 PNG SHA-256 `545e2e9f500e83947b8af6bd1b881187a25137932dcf05710e9ebc741814f5c3`.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `WindyDove`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg_marker_viewbox -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test pdf_test pdf_svg -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; showcase PDF render; Ghostscript page-3 rasterization and visual inspection; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-svg-marker-viewbox-profile-20260706T2210Z`; `sha256sum -c ../golden_checksums.txt` from the profile bundle's `golden/` directory.

- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a common SVG marker-viewport fidelity gap in the dependency-free PDF renderer while preserving existing no-viewBox marker behavior. The active goal remains open because `pdf-large` layout is still the dominant measured hotspot and the requested world-class SVG surface still has more coverage to add.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Text Stylesheet Presentation Cascade
- Timestamp: 2026-07-06T23:50:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T2336Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-text-css-cascade-20260706T2350Z/`.
- Current profile context: the fresh short gauntlet at `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T2336Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 297.120 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 24.732 ms p95, `html-large` third at 12.185 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.837 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.175 ms p95. The `pdf-large` stage profile still ranks `layout` first at 223.069 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 40.711 ms p95 and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.108 ms p95. The profile bundle's golden checksums all validated.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. This is primarily SVG/PDF fidelity rather than a claimed speed win, but it targets a common generated-SVG surface: text presentation properties provided through stylesheet selectors instead of repeated per-node attributes. Source tracing showed stylesheet rules already matched text nodes for fill, font family, font weight, dominant baseline, and letter spacing, but `font-size` and `text-anchor` were parsed through a separate attribute-only path.
- Root cause fixed: `parse_svg_text_elements` computed SVG text placement from `font-size` and `text-anchor` attributes plus inline declarations only. Matched stylesheet declarations such as `.label { font-size: 20px; text-anchor: middle; }` were ignored even though the same rule machinery correctly applied paint and font-face properties. For external SVG generators, this can make labels too small and left-aligned in PDF while the HTML/browser SVG renders them at the intended size and anchor.
- Renderer change: text parsing now resolves a scoped CSS-variable environment for each `<text>` and `<tspan>`, applies presentation attributes first, matched stylesheet rules in specificity/source order next, and inline style last for `font-size` and `text-anchor`. CSS `font-size` values support variables plus `em`, `ex`, percent, and point-like numeric units relative to the inherited text size. Existing presentation-attribute behavior for numeric values with unit suffixes remains preserved to avoid changing the pinned `font-size="20em"` compatibility fixture.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_text_stylesheet_font_size_and_anchor_affect_selectable_text` proves stylesheet `font-size` overrides a smaller presentation attribute, CSS-variable `text-anchor: middle` shifts the emitted selectable PDF text matrix, `tspan` stylesheet `font-size: 0.5em` resolves relative to the parent text size, and inline `font-size` still has final priority over matched stylesheet rules.
- First-principles proof: this changes only text placement/style resolution for `font-size` and `text-anchor` when a matched stylesheet or inline CSS declaration exists. SVG geometry, path painting, marker rendering, gradients, filters, masks/clips, text glyph shaping, font subsetting, PDF object ordering, compression, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. Existing SVG presentation-attribute numeric parsing remains intact, as proven by the restored `pdf_svg_numeric_attributes_accept_e_prefixed_unit_suffixes` fixture.
- frankenmermaid visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` through the normal file-input auto-asset path to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-svg-text-css-cascade-20260706T2350Z/showcase.pdf`, then rasterized page 3 through Ghostscript from `/tmp` because this Ghostscript build refused `/data/...` paths under its sandbox. Visual inspection of `page-03.png` shows the frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank, centered, colorful, and readable; node labels, routed arrows, arrowheads, dashed edge, Mermaid source block, and the following `Blockquotes` section all remain cleanly visible. Artifact hashes: `showcase.pdf` SHA-256 `946f220cf76d725ca8d40f22cef78b5efdf305714406416fea39d2688fc06015`; `page-03.png` SHA-256 `f30f1d55fc63c622217dcc68e2230ee34629fbdc319b9eeff54075d811938e29`.

## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Paragraph Builder Token-Map Allocation
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T00:20:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-builder-prealloc-after-20260707T0000Z/`, and final proof bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-builder-inline-groups-after-20260707T0015Z/`.
- Current profile context: the previous fresh profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260706T2336Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 297.120 ms p95, with the `layout` stage first at 223.069 ms p95. That makes PDF paragraph construction and line breaking the dominant measured hot path; serialization and page stream generation remain secondary.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 2, score 5.0. Source tracing showed the PDF-private paragraph builder still allocated three growable parallel maps from empty for every paragraph, and the common one-token-word path moved the reusable `word` vector into `item_toks`, losing its allocation on every word. This is pure allocation churn inside the layout stage and does not affect Knuth-Plass scoring.
- Rejected/avoided larger target: changing `build_segs_adjusted` to accumulate per-token widths without reshaping the merged same-style segment would be faster but not behavior-neutral. The existing code deliberately reshapes merged text so cross-token ligatures and kerning, such as `f` + `i`, affect the segment width; `pdf_segments_remeasure_merged_text_after_cross_token_shaping` pins that behavior.
- Renderer change: `BuiltParagraph` now pre-sizes `items`, `item_toks`, and `break_toks` from `toks.len() + 1`. The token map now stores each paragraph item as a compact `TokGroup` with an inline first token plus an optional rest vector. Ordinary one-token words and glue spaces therefore avoid a per-item `Vec<Tok>` allocation, while multi-token styled or split hyphenation fragments still preserve the old ordered token vector path. `line_tokens_for_break_into` expands `TokGroup` back into the same `LineTok` stream in item order.
- Regression target: `pdf_paragraph_builder_presizes_maps_from_token_count` pins the capacity preallocation and the three-map length invariant. Existing `pdf_word_measurement_uses_gpos_kerning`, `pdf_word_measurement_uses_gsub_ligature_advances`, and `pdf_segments_remeasure_merged_text_after_cross_token_shaping` continue to prove width semantics and cross-token shaping are unchanged.
- First-principles proof: the line breaker still sees the same `ParagraphItem` sequence and the same measured `TextBox.width` values. Rendering still receives the same tokens in the same order, with the same slots, links, strikethrough flags, and glue adjustments. The change removes container allocation shape only; ordering, tie-breaking, floating-point layout math, hyphenation points, selected breaks, PDF object ordering, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Behavior/performance proof: the final profile bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-pdf-builder-inline-groups-after-20260707T0015Z/` validates every golden checksum. `pdf-large.pdf` matches the previous current-profile SHA-256 exactly at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, and `parser-large.html` remains `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`. The final short gauntlet reports `pdf-large` p95 296.593 ms and mean 296.149 ms; `layout` p95 is 227.443 ms. This is recorded as a real allocation cleanup with directional timing in the same-host noise band, not a large latency claim.

## Fresh-Eyes Peer-Code Review - SVG Numeric Entity Safety
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T00:08:39Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Review scope: broad peer-code audit using `codebase-audit` plus `multi-pass-bug-hunting`. Re-read AGENTS/README, ran UBS once (summary-only output), scanned security/performance/CLI/filesystem patterns, traced the auto PDF image loader, staged writer, HTML/PDF URL sanitizers, WASM demo sandboxing, and the recent SVG/PDF renderer code. Most suspected issues were already covered by existing tests; the real defect found was in the SVG-only XML entity decoder.
- Root cause fixed: `decode_xml_entities` silently dropped malformed numeric entities such as `&#x;` and invalid numeric scalars such as `&#xD800;` or out-of-range decimal references. It also allowed `&#0;` to become a raw NUL character. Because ASCII PDF strings are emitted as literal `(...)` strings, an SVG root `<title>`/`<desc>` containing `&#0;` could place a raw NUL into `/Alt` text, while other invalid numeric references lost user-visible content entirely. The Markdown parser already handles this class correctly by mapping invalid numeric references to U+FFFD.
- Renderer change: SVG numeric XML references now decode through a small validated helper. Valid decimal and hex entities, including uppercase `#X`, still decode normally. XML-invalid numeric scalars, surrogates, NUL, and numeric overflow become U+FFFD. Malformed numeric spellings and unknown named entities remain literal instead of disappearing.
- Regression targets: private writer tests pin valid decimal/hex decoding, invalid numeric replacement, NUL rejection, uppercase hex handling, and preservation of malformed/unknown entity text. The public PDF regression `pdf_svg_accessible_text_replaces_invalid_numeric_entities_without_dropping_text` proves root SVG title/desc metadata reaches `/Alt` as a UTF-16BE PDF string with U+FFFD substitutions and literal malformed text.
- First-principles proof: valid SVG entity behavior is unchanged for the standard named entities plus well-formed decimal/hex numeric references. The change only affects malformed numeric spellings and XML-invalid numeric scalars, replacing unsafe data loss/control-byte emission with deterministic visible replacement or literal preservation. SVG parsing, geometry, marker rendering, image loading, HTML output, compression, PDF object ordering, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `YellowRiver`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; coordination message sent to recent related Agent Mail identities; `cargo test -q --lib svg_xml_entity_decoder`; `cargo test -q --test pdf_test pdf_svg_accessible_text_replaces_invalid_numeric_entities_without_dropping_text`; `cargo test -q --test pdf_test pdf_svg_root_title_and_desc_backfill_empty_markdown_alt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`.
- Coordination note: no commit was created because the shared checkout remains broadly dirty with peer work across docs, scripts, core modules, tests, examples, generated artifacts, and the active progress ledger. The accepted code edits for this pass are limited to SVG numeric XML entity safety and the focused regressions.
- Verdict: CLEAN AFTER FIX; this removes a concrete data-loss/control-character bug in peer-written SVG/PDF entity handling without broad churn. The active broader performance/SVG goal remains open.

## Fresh-Eyes Peer-Code Review - PDF Layout Width Cache and Script Safety Audit
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T00:32:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-width-cache-after-20260707T0022Z/`.
- Review scope: re-read AGENTS/README, applied `multi-pass-bug-hunting`, ran UBS against the dirty Rust diff and then narrowed to `src/pdf.rs`, manually traced the freshly modified PDF paragraph/token/segment flow, and sampled the peer-written run-id/archive-hardening scripts (`scripts/validate-run-id.sh`, artifact scripts, e2e scripts, `install.sh`, and `install.ps1`). The run-id validation is before artifact path construction/cleanup in the sampled scripts, archive extraction rejects traversal/link entries before install, changed Bash scripts parse with `bash -n`, and the source-shape tests for run-id ordering pass.
- Root cause fixed: the earlier single-token fast path removed one avoidable allocation but still left the dominant PDF layout stage repeatedly reshaping identical text fragments. Paragraph breaking, glue construction, hyphen penalty width, and final segment construction all asked `Faces::shaped_width` for the same `(font slot, font size, text)` values many times within one render. Because `Faces::shaped_width` performs deterministic GSUB/GPOS shaping and depends only on those inputs, the repeated calls were pure recomputation.
- Renderer change: `LayoutCx` now owns a render-local bounded `WidthCache` keyed by `(font slot, font size)` and text. PDF paragraph word measurement, interword glue, discretionary hyphen width, and positioned segment width calculation use the cache in the layout path. The fallback public/private helper path without a `LayoutCx` still calls `Faces::shaped_width` directly. The cache is dropped after each render, has a fixed entry cap, does not use globals or threads, and stores exactly the same `LayoutUnit` values returned by the old path.
- First-principles proof: the cache changes lookup mechanics only. It does not alter tokenization, hyphenation points, paragraph items, demerit scoring, selected breaks, segment grouping, floating-point coordinate math, emitted text, PDF object ordering, fonts, SVG rendering, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, or WASM portability. On a miss, it computes the old value first; on a hit, it returns that previously computed value for the same slot, size, and text within the same render.
- Behavior/performance proof: the fresh pre-cache profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0012Z/` ranked `pdf-large` first at 294.453 ms p95 with `layout` at 223.739 ms p95. The earlier single-token-only focused run was noisy/slower at 302.652 ms p95 and is superseded by the width-cache proof. The accepted focused 10-iteration after run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-width-cache-after-20260707T0022Z/` reports `pdf-large` p95 155.151 ms and mean 152.663 ms, with `layout` p95 79.993 ms. Its `golden/pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 is still `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, exactly matching the fresh pre-cache profile.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `SapphireCrane`; exclusive reservations for `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `src/pdf.rs`, and the relevant perf artifact directories; read-only peer recommendation from `Helmholtz` to add a render-local shaped-width cache; `ubs --diff --only=rust --format=jsonl --ci --skip-size-check`; targeted `ubs --files=src/pdf.rs --only=rust --format=text --ci --skip-size-check .`; `bash -n` over changed shell scripts; `cargo fmt`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo test pdf_word_measurement --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_paragraph_builder_presizes_maps_from_token_count --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_pdf_render_matches_normal_bytes_and_reports_required_stages --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test script_sources_test -- --nocapture`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs .skill-loop-progress.md`.

## Fresh-Eyes Peer-Code Review - Parser Reference Table Boundary Scan
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T00:43:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-local-table-after-20260707T0031Z/`.
- Review scope: applied `codebase-audit` and `multi-pass-bug-hunting` to the dirty shared checkout, with emphasis on high-risk peer-written parser/PDF/script surfaces rather than only the newest diff. UBS over the full dirty Rust diff emitted aggregate counts only; targeted text scans of `src/parse/mod.rs` and `src/pdf.rs` produced actionable output but the apparent criticals were triaged as false positives or test-only inventory. The `src/parse/mod.rs` "JWT" hit is a parser entity-decoder test named `valid_references_still_decode`, the `src/pdf.rs` "secret comparison" hit is a public PNG signature check, and the shown unwrap/panic hits are test assertions.
- Current profile context: fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z` ranked `pdf-large` first at 153.302 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 23.235 ms p95, `html-large` third at 12.937 ms p95, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.365 ms p95, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 4.990 ms p95. In `parser-large`, `reference_collection` remained a visible parser cost with p95 4.520 ms in the three-iteration fresh profile.
- Root cause fixed: reference-definition stripping still precomputed a full `table_end_boundaries(lines)` vector whenever any reference definition line was consumed. That helper tried every possible table start in the document to support one rare semantic case: preserving a blank line when a consumed reference-definition run separates adjacent table-like regions. On large documents with definitions, this added avoidable whole-document table probing to both normal parsing and spanned parsing.
- Parser change: replaced the eager global table-boundary sweep with a local `table_ends_at(lines, idx)` check that runs only on the first line of a consumed reference-definition run. The local check scans backward over the contiguous pipe-row region before the consumed run and tests each plausible table start with the same `table_extent` logic, so it preserves the table-boundary behavior without allocating or scanning unrelated document regions. `collect_top_level_spans` and `strip_consumed_references` now share this local check.
- Regression target: `local_table_end_detection_tolerates_prior_non_table_pipe_text` pins the important edge case where non-table pipe text precedes a real table, ensuring the local backward scan still finds the actual table start and does not confuse earlier pipe text with table structure. Existing `a_definition_between_adjacent_tables_preserves_the_table_boundary`, parser conformance, and span tests cover the user-visible behavior.
- First-principles proof: reference labels, title parsing, nested reference collection, paragraph-boundary semantics, table parsing, spanned source offsets, inline parsing, renderer output, filesystem behavior, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change removes an eager auxiliary allocation and broad scan; on the only branch that needs table-boundary knowledge, it asks the same table recognizer whether a table ends exactly at the consumed-run boundary.
- Behavior/performance proof: focused 10-iteration `parser-large` after-run reports p95 22.486 ms and mean 22.373 ms, with `reference_collection` p95 3.871 ms. The before/after samples are not directly identical in iteration count, so this is recorded as a focused directional improvement rather than a broad latency claim. The pre-change and post-change `parser-large.html` SHA-256 values are both `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`, and `sha256sum -c tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-local-table-after-20260707T0031Z/SHA256SUMS` validated the output and stage artifact.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `SapphireCrane`; exclusive reservations for `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and the two parser perf artifact directories; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z`; focused `release-perf` `fmd_perf_harness --scenario parser-large --iters 10`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test local_table_end_detection_tolerates_prior_non_table_pipe_text --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test a_definition_between_adjacent_tables_preserves_the_table_boundary --lib -- --nocapture`; `cargo test profiled_parser_matches_normal_ast_and_reports_required_stages --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --lib refdef_paragraph_tests -- --nocapture`; targeted UBS scans for `src/parse/mod.rs` and `src/pdf.rs`; Bash syntax check over changed shell scripts; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs .skill-loop-progress.md tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0031Z tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-local-table-after-20260707T0031Z`.

TJ ET` operator and also built a separate temporary `String` for the `TJ` glyph array. ## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Pattern `href` Inheritance
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T01:13:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0109Z/`, and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase.pdf`.
- Current profile context: fresh `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0109Z` ranks `pdf-large` first at 148.346 ms p95, followed by `parser-large` at 21.883 ms, `html-large` at 12.614 ms, `pdf-showcase` at 11.159 ms, and `compress-corpus` at 4.994 ms. PDF stage evidence now shows `layout` at 83.725 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 35.054 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.830 ms p95, and page-stream compression at roughly 18.782 ms per render by total stage time. This pass advances the SVG/PDF renderer fidelity requirement rather than claiming a speed win.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. The renderer already supported vector pattern tiling and gradient `href` inheritance, but generated SVGs commonly factor pattern geometry and tile content through `<pattern href="#base">` / `xlink:href`. Supporting that model reuses the existing dependency-free tiler and closes a common paint-server gap without adding external dependencies.
- Root cause fixed: `parse_svg_pattern_paints` parsed only direct, non-self-closing `<pattern>` elements that themselves declared `patternUnits="userSpaceOnUse"`, dimensions, and child geometry. A derived pattern such as `<pattern id="derived" href="#base" x="3"/>` therefore failed to inherit the base pattern's dimensions/body and could render as an unresolved solid fallback or disappear even though the base geometry was otherwise fully supported.
- Renderer change: added bounded pattern-definition collection and resolution, mirroring the existing gradient inheritance approach. Pattern definitions now resolve `href` / `xlink:href` chains up to a fixed depth, inherit missing attributes from the referenced pattern, inherit the referenced body only when the derived pattern has no child content, preserve first-definition-wins ordering, and then feed the resolved pattern into the existing vector child parser and tiler.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_patterns_inherit_attrs_and_body_via_href` pins `xlink:href` inheritance of base geometry/body, derived attribute overrides, and the case where a derived pattern supplies its own child body while keeping inherited geometry. The broader `pdf_svg` suite now includes 78 SVG/PDF tests covering patterns, gradients, masks, markers, text, CSS, transforms, opacity, and image handling.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` to `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase.pdf` with `SOURCE_DATE_EPOCH=1700000000`, copied it to `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase.pdf`, rasterized pages 3-4 with Ghostscript, and visually inspected `/tmp/fmd-showcase-review-pattern-href-20260707T0111Z/showcase-page-01.png` and `showcase-page-02.png`. The frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank and readable, with vector-looking colored boxes, routed arrows, the dashed edge, and legible labels; the following page still shows visible Rust/Python/JSON/shell syntax highlighting.
- Isomorphism proof: SVGs without pattern `href` still take the same direct pattern parse/draw path; unresolved or unsupported patterns still fail closed through existing fallback behavior; derived patterns only reuse attributes/body that SVG paint servers define as inherited through references; pattern tiling, child geometry parsing, CSS matching, PDF operators, floating-point formatting, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability remain on existing code paths.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `OliveDesert`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and the fresh profile artifact; `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-current-profile-20260707T0109Z`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo test pdf_svg_patterns_inherit_attrs_and_body_via_href --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg --test pdf_test -- --nocapture`; `git diff --check -- src/pdf.rs tests/pdf_test.rs`; showcase PDF render plus Ghostscript rasterization and visual inspection; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`; `cargo check --no-default-features`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG pattern paint-server gap while keeping the renderer dependency-free and visually verified against the real frankenmermaid showcase. The active goal remains open because broader world-class SVG coverage and continued profile-driven optimization are still larger than this focused pass.
