## Active Goal Continuation - PDF Layout Cache Trial Rejections
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T02:22:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `.skill-loop-progress.md` only. Two `src/pdf.rs` optimization trials were implemented, tested, measured, and fully reverted because both were performance-negative despite preserving PDF bytes.
- Current profile context: the fresh `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0202Z/` bundle ranks `pdf-large` first at 143.966 ms p95, with PDF `layout` at 83.738 ms p95, `page_content_stream_generation` at 28.629 ms p95, `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 23.473 ms p95, and `page_stream_compression` at 260.252 us p95 per stream. `pdf-large.pdf` SHA-256 is `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`.
- Rejected trial 1: changed `build_segs_adjusted` to measure growing same-style line segment prefixes exactly without inserting those prefixes into the render-local width cache. Hypothesis: prefix strings are mostly unique and cache insertion is overhead. Evidence rejected the hypothesis: the 10-iteration baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-segbuild-baseline-20260707T0222Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 142.595 ms and layout p95 84.037 ms, while the post-change artifact `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-segbuild-after-20260707T0222Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 258.408 ms and layout p95 192.092 ms. Both artifacts kept `pdf-large.pdf` byte-identical at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`, proving the rejection is performance-only. Conclusion: the growing-prefix width cache is materially useful for this corpus and must not be bypassed casually.
- Rejected trial 2: replaced the raw nested `WidthCache` map with a private struct that tracked total entry count in O(1), avoiding the old `cache.values().map(HashMap::len).sum()` on cache misses. Hypothesis: cache-size recounting was hot bookkeeping. Evidence did not support keeping it: the same baseline reported `pdf-large` p95 142.595 ms and layout p95 84.037 ms, while `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-widthcache-after-20260707T0222Z/` reported `pdf-large` p95 144.566 ms and layout p95 88.033 ms. The output hash again stayed byte-identical at `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`. Conclusion: this bookkeeping change is inside the variance/noise envelope at best and slightly negative in the focused run; leave the simpler existing map shape in place.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `WildHill`; released stale self-reservations from `BlackCove`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-layout-segbuild-*`; focused baseline and two focused `release-perf` post-change runs; focused PDF writer tests during each trial; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo fmt --check`; final `git diff -- src/pdf.rs` is empty after reverting both rejected trials.
- Verdict: ZERO-CODE-CHANGE REJECTION PASS; no production code should be committed from these two attempts. The useful outcome is a negative hypothesis ledger that prevents future agents from repeating two tempting but harmful PDF layout/cache edits. The active goal remains open; next useful optimization work should target layout with deeper attribution than cache-shape guessing, or move to a different measured top-five surface.

## Active Goal Continuation - DEFLATE Match Symbol Lookup Tables
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T02:35:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/compress.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf artifacts under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-*` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the fresh `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0202Z/` bundle ranks `compress-corpus` fifth at 5.034 ms p95 and shows PDF `page_stream_compression` at 260.252 us p95 per page stream, with 252 page streams over the three-iteration profile. This is below the dominant PDF layout work but is a clean low-hanging path shared by PDF page streams, embedded font streams, PNG fixture generation, and standalone compression users.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. Source tracing showed every emitted LZ77 match searched the static DEFLATE length and distance base tables with reverse linear scans, even though the mapping from legal match length 3..=258 and distance 1..=32768 to RFC 1951 symbols is immutable.
- Compressor change: added compile-time lookup generation for match length symbols and a 32 KiB static distance-symbol table, then changed `emit_match` to index those tables instead of searching `LENGTH_BASE` and `DIST_BASE` for every match. The existing base and extra-bit tables remain the source of truth for emitted extra-bit payloads and for inflater decoding. No dependency, unsafe code, global mutable state, threading, filesystem, process, or native-runtime assumption was introduced.
- Regression target: `match_symbol_tables_preserve_search_mapping` exhaustively compares the new length and distance tables against the old highest-base-less-than-or-equal search for every legal value. The existing roundtrip sweeps still cover empty, text, binary, stored fallback, max-length matches, self-overlap, window-edge distances, and production inflater paths.
- First-principles proof: LZ77 match finding, literal emission, Huffman code tables, extra-bit values, stored-block fallback, zlib headers, Adler-32, decompression, PDF object ordering, page-content bytes before compression, font subsetting, SVG/image paths, parser behavior, HTML output, WASM portability, and deterministic output policy are unchanged. The accepted change only replaces a pure symbol-selection search with a table generated by the same search at compile time.
- Behavior/performance proof: the focused baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-baseline-20260707T0235Z/` reported `compress-corpus` p95 6.083 ms and mean 5.159 ms over 20 iterations, with output size 107098 B. The exact final-source longer sample `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-final100-20260707T0235Z/` reported p95 5.029 ms and mean 4.806 ms over 100 iterations, with the same output size, and `compress-corpus.lengths` is byte-identical to the baseline. A 20-iteration final-source sample had one high p95 outlier at 6.258 ms despite mean 5.020 ms, so the retained claim is based on the longer sample plus downstream PDF evidence rather than that noisy p95.
- PDF proof: the focused `pdf-large` baseline `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-pdfbaseline-20260707T0235Z/` reported p95 141.320 ms and mean 140.256 ms over five iterations. The exact final-source `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-pdffinal-20260707T0235Z/` reported p95 137.765 ms and mean 135.988 ms over five iterations. `pdf-large.pdf` stayed byte-identical at SHA-256 `11b4e0f2e1ae6f3b18dcae8ec20e9df5be3c447fd0875607e0ce5d731edbcfd1`; `page_stream_compression` p95 moved from 274.088 us to 256.144 us and `font_stream_compression` p95 from 123.764 us to 68.960 us in the focused stage ledgers.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `WildHill`; exclusive reservations for `src/compress.rs`, `tests/*compress*`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-compress-matchtables-*`; focused baseline and final `release-perf` runs for `compress-corpus` and `pdf-large`; direct `sha256sum` comparison for pre/post `pdf-large.pdf`; direct diff of pre/post `compress-corpus.lengths`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo fmt --check`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo test compress::tests --lib`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo check --all-targets`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `RUSTUP_TOOLCHAIN=1.95.0-x86_64-unknown-linux-gnu cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/compress.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this is a byte-preserving, dependency-free compressor hot-path cleanup with exhaustive symbol-mapping coverage and measurable benefit in both standalone compression and PDF stream serialization. The active broader goal remains open because PDF layout is still the dominant measured hotspot and the requested SVG/mermaid renderer scope extends beyond this compression pass.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Object-Bounding-Box Clip And Mask Units
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T03:12:00Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`.
- Current profile context: the previous fresh broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0245Z/` still ranks `pdf-large` first at 143.455 ms p95 and shows SVG/PDF fidelity as a parallel project goal rather than the dominant CPU hotspot. This pass intentionally targets a correctness gap in the dependency-free SVG renderer: generated SVGs and authoring tools commonly use `clipPathUnits="objectBoundingBox"` and `maskContentUnits="objectBoundingBox"`.
- Root cause fixed: parsed clip paths and supported hard-mask geometry stored only raw path operations plus fill rule. At draw time every clip/mask path was emitted as user-space geometry, so object-bounding-box definitions stayed in 0..1 coordinates instead of being scaled and translated into the target element's bbox. That made common normalized masks/clips either invisible or far too small.
- Renderer change: added explicit unit metadata to parsed `SvgClipPath` definitions, parsing `clipPathUnits` for clip paths and `maskContentUnits` for masks with SVG-correct user-space defaults. Shape, embedded-image, and selectable-text clipping now pass target bboxes into a shared applicability/emission helper. User-space clips remain allocation-free; object-bounding-box clips clone and transform only the small referenced clip path, and degenerate target bboxes fail closed instead of emitting malformed PDF geometry.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_object_bounding_box_clip_and_mask_units_scale_to_target_geometry` pins exact PDF clipping geometry for normalized clip and mask definitions scaled onto rectangle targets. Existing user-space clip, mask, and transformed child clip tests were rerun to prove the old behavior stayed intact.
- First-principles proof: SVG parsing, style inheritance, fill/stroke paint, gradients, patterns, marker rendering, image embedding, selectable text emission, PDF object numbering, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged. The change only alters the coordinate transform applied to already-supported clip/mask geometry when an SVG definition explicitly requests object-bounding-box content units.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `QuietBarn`; exclusive reservations for `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; `cargo test pdf_svg_object_bounding_box_clip_and_mask_units_scale_to_target_geometry -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_clip -- --nocapture`; `cargo test pdf_svg_masks -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; full `cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this closes a concrete SVG/PDF fidelity gap without adding dependencies or changing the fast user-space clip path. The active broader goal remains open because there are still larger SVG feature and PDF-layout performance surfaces beyond this focused pass.

The broad after-run reports `html-code-heavy` p95 2.760 ms versus 3.618 ms before; the focused 20-iteration after-run reports `html-code-heavy` p95 3.145 ms and byte-identical output. `html-large` moved only 2.0% in the broad p95 comparison, so this pass claims a targeted highlighted-code improvement rather than a material full-HTML-render speedup.

## Active Goal Continuation - Parser Plain Multiline Paragraph Fast Path
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T03:47:24Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf bundles under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-multiline-*` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the current-main profile `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T032710Z/` ranked `parser-large` second at 23.460 ms p95, and parser stage attribution showed `inline_parse` at 4.158 us p95 per invocation with `paragraph_block` at 8.466 us p95. That made paragraph inline handoff a plausible lower-risk target after the recent PDF layout cache trials were rejected.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 3, confidence 5, effort 1, score 15.0. Source tracing showed multi-line paragraphs always materialized a `Vec<char>` and entered the full inline parser solely to turn `\n` into soft/hard break inline nodes, even when each component line was otherwise plain text. The existing single-line `plain_inline_fast_path` already proved the syntax-free case can skip delimiter/link parsing.
- Parser change: `parse_lines_as_inlines` now detects multi-line paragraphs whose component lines individually need no full inline parse, then emits the exact `Inline::Text`, `Inline::SoftBreak`, and trailing-two-space `Inline::HardBreak` sequence directly. It preserves full parser fallback for any line containing inline syntax, escapes, links, bare URLs/emails, entities, HTML/autolinks, code spans, emphasis, strike, or images. Non-final line trailing spaces are stripped exactly like the existing newline branch in the full parser; the final line is preserved.
- Regression targets: `plain_multiline_paragraph_preserves_soft_and_hard_breaks` pins soft-break trimming plus two-space hard-break behavior. `multiline_paragraph_with_inline_syntax_uses_full_inline_parser` pins that mixed paragraphs still resolve emphasis after a soft break. The pre-existing `multiline_paragraph_inline_handoff_preserves_soft_breaks_and_references` fixture was rerun as an additional guard.
- Behavior/performance proof: the focused after-run `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-multiline-plain-after2-20260707T0340Z/` reported `parser-large` p95 19.550 ms and mean 19.170 ms over 50 iterations, with `parser-large.html` byte-identical to the current-main profile (`951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`). To control for current host drift, a detached clean-HEAD worktree at `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_baseline_20260707T0340Z` rebuilt the old source and reported `parser-large` p95 23.407 ms and mean 22.894 ms over 50 iterations. The same clean-HEAD cross-check showed `html-large` p95 16.835 ms versus current-source p95 15.394 ms, confirming the earlier 3-iteration broad HTML p95 noise was not caused by this parser change.
- Broad profile proof: `scripts/perf-gauntlet.sh --iters 3 --run-id continue-parser-multiline-plain-profile-20260707T0340Z` completed, validated all golden checksums, kept `pdf-large` as the top p95 hotspot, and reported `parser-large` p95 22.551 ms versus 23.460 ms in the current-main bundle. `scripts/perf-compare.sh` flagged unrelated 3-sample p95 noise in pre-parsed HTML/PDF showcase scenarios; the focused clean-HEAD cross-check above is the stronger attribution evidence for this one-lever parser change.
- First-principles proof: block parsing, reference collection, table/list/blockquote logic, inline syntax semantics, HTML/PDF renderers, SVG/Mermaid paths, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, filesystem behavior, WASM portability, and deterministic output policy are unchanged. The accepted change only replaces a pure syntax-free multi-line paragraph tokenization path with direct construction of the same inline nodes.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `QuietBarn`; exclusive reservations for `src/parse/mod.rs`, `tests/parser_conformance.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`; `cargo fmt`; focused new parser tests; `cargo test refdef_paragraph_tests --lib -- --nocapture`; full `cargo test --test parser_conformance -- --nocapture`; `RUSTFLAGS="-C force-frame-pointers=yes" cargo build --profile release-perf --example fmd_perf_harness`; focused current-source parser/html/pdf samples; detached clean-HEAD baseline build and focused parser/html samples; direct SHA-256 comparisons for parser/html outputs; `cargo fmt --check && cargo check --all-targets && cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings && cargo check --no-default-features --lib && cargo test`; `git diff --check -- src/parse/mod.rs tests/parser_conformance.rs`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes avoidable parser allocation/state-machine work for common plain multi-line paragraphs with byte-identical rendered output and a same-host focused parser p95 improvement of roughly 16.5%. ## Active Goal Continuation - HTML Font Usage ASCII Bitset
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T04:02:50Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/html.rs` and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated perf bundles under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-font-bitset-*` and the detached baseline worktree `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_html_bitset_baseline_20260707T0357Z` are evidence only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: the latest broad bundle `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-parser-multiline-plain-profile-20260707T0340Z/` ranks `html-large` third overall at 15.459 ms p95, behind `pdf-large` and `parser-large`. Recent PDF table-width cache and parser reference-candidate trials were rejected by measurement, making the pre-parsed HTML/font path a lower-risk top-five target for this pass.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 4, effort 1, score 8.0. Source tracing showed HTML font usage collection stored the ASCII subset as `[bool; 128]` plus a separate `has_ascii` flag. Large documents repeatedly OR character membership into that array before every HTML font subset. A compact bitset should reduce per-slot state size and write traffic while preserving the same deterministic ASCII-before-non-ASCII character ordering.
- Renderer change: `FontCharSet` now stores ASCII membership as a `u128` mask and keeps non-ASCII membership in the existing `BTreeSet<char>`. ASCII text extends a local mask and ORs it into the slot once; `to_chars` emits set ASCII bits in ascending byte order, then extends with the ordered non-ASCII set exactly as before.
- First-principles proof: font slot selection, seed characters, non-ASCII ordering, `@font-face` emission, TrueType parsing/subsetting, base64 encoding, HTML body rendering, syntax highlighting, PDF output, SVG/Mermaid paths, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, filesystem behavior, and WASM portability are unchanged. This changes only the internal set representation used to compute the same per-slot keep-character lists.
- Behavior proof: clean-baseline `html-large.html` and trial `html-large.html` both have SHA-256 `951798518c0720d7f3df4995b128a5729839abba83662e0e6de60a5d6ecdf74f`; clean-baseline `html-code-heavy.html` and trial `html-code-heavy.html` both have SHA-256 `e7ac126b62e87ea39051f2eee4f1d5031fd2f998bec3a115d951843e54544b40`. Direct `cmp -s` checks reported `html-large-identical` and `html-code-heavy-identical`.
- Performance proof: initial current-source `html-large` baseline over 50 iterations reported p95 15.805 ms and mean 14.700 ms. The first trial run over 50 iterations was flat/slightly worse at p95 15.851 ms and mean 14.828 ms, so a stronger clean-baseline comparison was taken. A detached clean `HEAD` worktree at `/data/tmp/franken_markdown_html_bitset_baseline_20260707T0357Z` reported `html-large` p95 15.335 ms and mean 14.465 ms over 100 iterations; the trial reported p95 14.942 ms and mean 13.871 ms over 100 iterations. `html-code-heavy` clean baseline reported p95 2.507 ms and mean 2.413 ms; the trial reported p95 2.440 ms and mean 2.417 ms. This is accepted as a byte-preserving directional cleanup, not a major latency claim because the p95 movement is below the 10% variance threshold.
- Verification: Agent Mail registration as `QuietBarn`; exclusive reservations for `src/html.rs`, `.skill-loop-progress.md`, and `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-html-font-bitset-*`; focused current and clean-baseline release-perf harness runs; direct SHA-256 and `cmp -s` output comparisons; `cargo test --lib html::tests::font_char_set_keeps_btree_character_order -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --lib html::tests -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test smoke_test default_html_embeds_deterministic_subset_font_faces -- --nocapture`; `cargo test --test highlight_test -- --nocapture`; `cargo fmt --check`; `cargo check --all-targets`; `cargo clippy --all-targets -- -D warnings`; `cargo check --no-default-features --lib`; full `cargo test`.
- Verdict: PRODUCTIVE; this removes small but avoidable ASCII set memory traffic from the top-five pre-parsed HTML path while keeping generated HTML bytes identical. The active broader goal remains open because `pdf-large` remains the top measured hotspot and the requested dependency-free SVG/Mermaid renderer scope remains broader than this internal HTML cleanup.

## Active Goal Continuation - SVG Marker Child Paint Order
- Timestamp: 2026-07-07T04:32:27Z.
- Files changed this pass: `src/pdf.rs`, `tests/pdf_test.rs`, and `.skill-loop-progress.md`. Generated evidence under `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0428Z/` and `tests/artifacts/svg-showcase/continue-marker-paint-order-visual-20260707T0435Z/` is proof material only and should remain uncommitted.
- Current profile context: fresh current-HEAD gauntlet `tests/artifacts/perf/continue-current-profile-20260707T0428Z/` ranks `pdf-large` first at 147.863 ms p95, `parser-large` second at 21.917 ms, `html-large` third at 15.692 ms, `pdf-showcase` fourth at 10.145 ms, and `compress-corpus` fifth at 7.588 ms. PDF stage attribution keeps `layout` first at 85.147 ms p95, followed by `page_content_stream_generation` at 29.767 ms p95, `page_stream_compression` at 261 us per stream, and `pdf_object_serialization_total` at 24.589 ms p95. The bundle's golden checksums all validated.
- Opportunity matrix: impact 2, confidence 5, effort 1, score 10.0. A parser reference-candidate shortcut was explicitly avoided because the ledger already records that carried-flag variant as a rejected performance trial. This pass instead targets the active SVG renderer objective with a small correctness gap: outer line/path/poly marker layers honored `paint-order`, but child shapes inside a referenced `<marker>` still painted through the legacy combined fill/stroke operator.
- Root cause fixed: `append_svg_marker` resolved marker-context paint and shadow/transform state for each marker child, then always called `append_svg_style`, `append_svg_path_ops`, and `append_svg_paint_operator`. That path ignores `SvgStyle.paint_order`, so a marker child such as `<path fill=... stroke=... paint-order="stroke fill">` rendered like default fill-then-stroke in PDF even though browser SVG paints stroke before fill.
- Renderer change: marker child rendering now delegates to `append_svg_marker_shape_paint`. The default marker path stays byte/logic equivalent and keeps the compact combined `B`/`B*` operator. Only marker child shapes with non-normal `paint-order` and both fill and stroke expand into ordered fill and stroke layers; the marker-layer token itself is ignored inside marker children because nested markers are not a valid paint layer there.
- Regression target: `pdf_svg_paint_order_applies_inside_marker_child_shapes` proves a marker child with `paint-order="stroke fill"` emits the blue stroke layer before the red fill layer, while a sibling marker child without custom paint-order still emits the compact fill+stroke `B` operator.
- Visual proof: rendered `examples/showcase.md` through the normal file-input PDF path, relying on automatic sibling SVG loading for `examples/showcase-mermaid.svg`, then rasterized page 3 via Ghostscript using a `/tmp` copy because this Ghostscript build rejects direct `/data/...` reads under `-dSAFER`. Visual inspection of `page-03.png` shows the frankenmermaid diagram is nonblank, centered, colorful, and readable; node labels, routed arrows, arrowheads, the dashed Mermaid edge into `PDF`, the Mermaid source block, and the following `Blockquotes` section all remain visible. Artifact hashes: `showcase.pdf` SHA-256 `946f220cf76d725ca8d40f22cef78b5efdf305714406416fea39d2688fc06015`; `page-03.png` SHA-256 `739fc2e3b8cf955587042f5f1b877fb23f2641cf64a55187133c9bc8202176ba`.
- First-principles proof: the change is restricted to painting marker child paths after marker placement, viewBox, markerUnits, orient, context-paint, shadows, and graphics-state prefixing have already been resolved. Default marker children still use the same compact paint operator, so ordinary frankenmermaid marker output and normal shape rendering are unchanged. SVG parsing, marker placement/orientation, line/path/poly outer paint-order, gradients, patterns, masks/clips, PDF object numbering, compression, dependencies, unsafe-code policy, and WASM portability are unchanged.
